        updated: 2026-05-17 04:00:46 UTC

    Edit `Browser.update_data._apply` in `040-state.py` so the
    post-batch order becomes: apply ops → snapshot pre-vis →
    `_recompute_filter_hidden` → `_apply_hide_displacement` →
    `_apply_cursor_anchor`. The filter pass must run *before*
    hide-displacement so the post-batch visible list reflects
    filter-hidden rows. Test: streaming a new matching item unhides
    its scaffold parent; streaming a non-matching item under an
    optimistic parent flips the parent to hidden.

  * ## Ticket: Task: FILTER_EDIT keymap + dispatch {#373}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-17 03:40:43 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-17 04:04:16 UTC

    Add `_filter` action in `070-actions.py` bound to `&` (NORMAL
    entry: appends `''` placeholder, sets mode to FILTER_EDIT). Add
    FILTER_EDIT dispatch path in `dispatch_key`: handle Backspace,
    Enter (empty → clear all, non-empty → commit), Ctrl-X (clear all),
    Ctrl-C / Esc (cancel current edit), printable char (mutate last
    entry); everything else falls through to NORMAL dispatch (mirrors
    SEARCH_EDIT). Recompute fires after any keystroke that changes
    the last entry. Unit tests for each transition.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Status row indicator {#374}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-17 03:40:43 UTC

* ## Ticket: Task: (1) Recipe get_children reload arg: avoid blowing _TREE_CACHE on idempotent root re-fetch {#407}

      updated: 2026-05-20 06:04:06 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-20 05:54:24 UTC

  Recipe-side: change get_children(item_id) to accept get_children(item_id, *, reload=False). When item_id is None and reload is False, skip the _TREE_CACHE.clear() / _TAIL_STATE.clear() — just rebuild the projects listing. When reload is True (or via the existing ctx.refresh / Ctrl-R path), do the full wipe.

  Framework-side: thread the reload flag through whatever calls get_children(None) so refreshes pass reload=True and initial loads pass reload=False (default). Currently 040-state.py / 080-cli.py invokes get_children with one positional arg only.

  Backwards compat: callers that pass only one arg get reload=False (the safe default), so legacy recipes don't break. Recipes that don't accept the kwarg still work via inspect.signature() probing or a try/except fallback in the framework's dispatcher.

  Measured impact (from perf logs): cuts case-1 startup time roughly in half by eliminating the second cold _scan_tree (the one that fires at ~3.4s after _TREE_CACHE was wiped by the initial get_children(None) call).

  * ## Comments {#407:comments}

    * Implemented: get_children gains optional reload kwarg honoured at every id shape (None, .jsonl path, #prompt/tool/span umbrella ids, #agent: subagent ids). Framework's _do_refresh passes reload=True via a new _children_reload_pending set drained by the worker. Backwards compat: signature probed once at Browser construction; legacy recipes without the kwarg keep working. Two new tests cover the root-reload and subtree-reload paths; the previously-unconditional cache-wipe test updated to assert the new semantics. Eliminates the 3.4s second cold _scan_tree on startup observed in perf-296238.log. {#407:comment:409}

* ## Ticket: Task: (2) Unify expand pipeline: one get_children per expand; incremental preview update; consider streaming + cached visible children {#408}

      updated: 2026-05-28 21:55:55 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-20 05:54:24 UTC

  Problem: expanding a single umbrella triggers list_prompt_children 3x for the same id (~350ms each on a 496-item turn). The three callers are:
    1. Preview composition for the cursor row (get_preview -> _collect_umbrella_preview -> get_children).
    2. The do_expand worker fetch (cached=0).
    3. A subsequent preview re-pull on cursor jiggle.

  Goals:
    A. Single get_children per expand. Preview composition and tree extension must share the same result rather than each re-fetching. Either:
       - Route _collect_umbrella_preview through browser.cached_children() first and fall back only on miss.
       - Have the expand pipeline drive both: produce children -> apply_ops -> compose preview from the just-cached list.

    B. Incremental preview updates on append. Right now any tail-driven push regenerates the entire preview text. Detect append-only deltas and append the rendered tail rather than recomposing from scratch. Full recomposition only when an insertion / removal / reparent occurs.

    C. Cached visible-children list on the node. Maintain a memoized 'visible children' per umbrella keyed on (children list identity, hidden flags). Invalidate explicitly when any of those change. Cheap to read on every paint.

    D. (Open question) Convert _collect_umbrella_preview and possibly _list_prompt_children / _list_tool_children into generators that yield rendered chunks. Pair with the framework's streaming-push API (Browser.update_data generator path) so a slow expand surfaces rows / preview lines progressively instead of in a single batch.

  Measured baseline (from perf logs, prompt:27722 with 496 children):
    list_prompt_children 0.354s x 3 = ~1050ms total, ~700ms wasted on duplicates.
    Per-item cost in _list_prompt_children: ~700us/item — likely worth profiling _tree_item / _tool_umbrella_item to find easy wins, but secondary to dedup.

  Dependencies: ticket 407 (reload arg) is independent and should land first.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Preview cache on Item: eager invalidation + recipe-side eager-push during composition {#410}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-22 00:27:08 UTC

    Supersedes #411, #412, #413 (all closed as duplicates).

    ## Background

    Today's preview pipeline has three problems that compound:
      * Wrap recomputed on every paint. `render_preview` walks the full preview text through `_wrap_preview_line` on every keystroke (050-render.py:1568-1581). For multi-MB previews this dominates per-paint cost — observable as PgUp/PgDn lag.
      * Sidecar dict for preview. `_state._preview = {id: str}` is keyed by id and not tied to Item lifetime; orphans possible when items are removed via `update_data`.
      * Composer bypasses framework cache. `_collect_umbrella_preview` (recipes/browse-claude:3773) recursively calls the recipe's `get_children` directly, causing duplicate fetches (~350ms × 3 per expand on a 496-child umbrella) and per-record re-renders on every tail tick.

    ## Design

    Three connected pieces. Parts A and B are required; Part C is optional optimization.

    ### Part A — Framework: preview cache lives on Item

    Move preview storage from `_state._preview` (id-keyed dict) onto the Item itself:

    ```python
    class Item:
        ...
        preview: Optional[str] = None              # raw text (replaces _state._preview[id])
        preview_render: Optional[PreviewRender] = None  # wrapped form + tail offsets
    ```

    `PreviewRender` is a small namedtuple/dataclass:

    ```python
    PreviewRender = namedtuple('PreviewRender', [
        'wrapped',              # list[str] of pre-wrapped display rows
        'raw_tail_offset',      # index in raw text where the last partial/last raw line starts
        'wrapped_tail_offset',  # index in wrapped where that last raw line's wrap starts
    ])
    ```

    The offsets enable `append_preview` to extend the wrapped buffer in place without re-wrapping the whole preview.

    Eager invalidation hooks (each drops `Item.preview_render` to None; the wrap regenerates lazily on next paint):
      * `set_preview(id, text)` → set `item.preview = text`, `item.preview_render = None`
      * `clear_preview(id)` / `invalidate_preview(id)` → drop both
      * Terminal resize → walk loaded Items, set `preview_render = None` on each
      * `_toggle_preview_ansi` → same
      * `update_data` mod/upsert touching an Item → drop its `preview` and `preview_render` (item mutated, preview may be stale)

    `append_preview(id, chunk)` is the special case: extend `item.preview` with `chunk`, and if `item.preview_render` is present, extend the wrapped buffer in place — take `raw[raw_tail_offset:] + chunk`, split on `\n`, wrap each new raw line, replace `wrapped[wrapped_tail_offset:]` with the result, update both offsets.

    Lazy fill at render: `render_preview` reads `item.preview_render`; if `None`, generate by running `_sanitize_preview` then per-line `_wrap_preview_line` over `item.preview`, store the result. If width or ansi_on differs from cached values (defensive — eager invalidation should have dropped already), regenerate.

    Public API: `Browser.cached_preview(id) -> str | None` keeps returning the raw text (read from `item.preview`). Wrapped form stays framework-internal. Pager/editor consumers see no change.

    Search query: confirmed there is no visible search highlight in the preview pane today (`_write_highlighted` is never called from `render_preview`; the `drop_sgr` logic at 050-render.py:1572-1581 strips SGR for matching lines but no overlay is drawn — effectively dead code). The wrap cache key is just `(text identity, width, ansi_on)`; query changes never invalidate.

    ### Part B — Recipe: eager-push children during preview composition

    When `get_preview(umbrella_id)` runs in browse-claude:
      * The composer walks the umbrella's children to build the preview text.
      * Each discovered child is pushed to the framework via `ctx.update_data(upsert(...))` ops.
      * Recursion into nested umbrellas (`#tool:`, `#span:`, `#prompt:`) pushes those descendants too — single batched `update_data` call with the entire touched subtree.

    After composition, the previewed subtree is in `_state._children` / `_state._items_by_id`, indistinguishable from "expanded then collapsed". Verified safe:
      * Collapse logic (`_collapse_or_back` 070-actions.py:195-215, `_collapse_recursive` 070-actions.py:680-689) only mutates `state.expanded`, never `_state._children`.
      * Visible-tree projection gates on `child.id in state.expanded`, not on `_state._children` presence — so eager-pushed children stay hidden.

    Concrete consumer changes:
      * `_collect_umbrella_preview` reads children from `_BROWSER.cached_children(umbrella_id)` rather than calling `get_children` directly (subsumes the old #413).
      * Per-record render lives on `Item.preview`: composer reads `child.preview`, falls through to `_render_record_with_rule` on miss, writes back via `set_preview(child.id, rendered)`.
      * The umbrella's composed preview lives on the umbrella's own Item via the framework's standard `set_preview` path.

    ### Part C — Optional: records as Item extras, shrink `_TREE_CACHE`

    Recipe attaches raw JSON record to Item via custom-attr extras (`upsert(... record=raw_obj)`):
      * `_render_record_with_rule` reads `item.record` instead of `_TREE_CACHE.records[n]`.
      * `_TREE_CACHE` keeps indexes (`turn_direct`, `tool_children`, `agent_link`, `tool_to_turn_root_line`, `line_offsets`) and live-tail byte-offset state, but the records themselves move to Items.
      * `_TREE_CACHE` shrinks; reduces one indirection layer per render.

    Optional because Parts A + B already deliver the performance wins; Part C is cleanup that simplifies the data model.

    ## Side effects worth flagging

    Visible behavior changes from Part B:
      * Children grid pane (between list and preview, 050-render.py:1741) populates immediately for preview-loaded umbrellas — today it's empty for unexpanded ones. Probably a positive UX change but worth noting.
      * `cached_parents()` returns more entries (preview-touched umbrellas + their nested umbrellas). Recipes iterating "all loaded subtrees" may see growth.
      * Memory grows monotonically with preview navigation. Bounded by data size — for a 30k-record session, end state could be ~30k Items in `_items_by_id` after enough browsing.
      * First expand of a previewed umbrella is instant (cache hit, no fetch).
      * Tail-tick recompose is cheap (per-record cache hits for unchanged records).

    ## Wins

    * PgUp/PgDn lag on big previews → fixed (Part A wrap cache).
    * 3× duplicate `get_children` per expand → fixed (Part B routes through `cached_children`).
    * Tail-tick preview recompose → cheap (per-record cache on `Item.preview`, only new records render fresh).
    * Preview-cache lifetime tied to Item lifetime, no orphan tracking.

    ## Open implementation questions (resolve during build)

    * `Item` equality / hashability: ensure `preview` and `preview_render` are excluded from `__eq__` / `__hash__` if those exist; otherwise mutations break dict / set semantics.
    * `Item.preview` memory footprint: defer LRU bound to a follow-up unless real-world testing shows pressure.
    * Per-Item `record` extras (Part C): ensure live-tail `update_data` `mod` ops update `item.record` when the record itself mutates (rare but possible).
    * `_BROWSER` singleton access from `get_preview`: already exists for preview-width lookup; just consume it in the composer.

    ## Subtickets

    Work breakdown follows in subtickets. Land in order — each builds on the previous.

    * ## Comments {#410:comments}

      * Closed: all non-future subtickets done. #422 (preview-on-Item + wrap cache), #423 (in-place append extension), #424 (composer routing + eager-push + per-leaf cache), #430 (registration-constraint docs + dead search-SGR removal), #431 (set_preview through post queue + single-flight verification). #425 (records-as-Item-extras) remains future. Commits: 1528948, aac2740, 4779c18, 1b76bb7, e962b20, fc1ea8d, b1cad98. {#410:comment:432}

    * ## Ticket: Framework: move preview storage to Item with eager-invalidated wrap cache {#422}

          status: done
          created: 2026-05-21 09:58:07 UTC
          updated: 2026-05-21 10:47:14 UTC

      Foundation subticket. Two commits expected.

      **Commit 1 — pure refactor:** replace `_state._preview = {id: str}` with `Item.preview: Optional[str]`. Update all readers/writers (~6 call sites including `set_preview`, `append_preview`, `clear_preview`, `invalidate_preview`, `cached_preview`, the pager/editor action, and the renderer). `cached_preview(id)` reads `items_by_id[id].preview if id in items_by_id else None`. Tests should still pass — no behavior change.

      **Commit 2 — wrap cache:** add `Item.preview_render: Optional[PreviewRender]`, a small namedtuple/dataclass:

      ```python
      PreviewRender = namedtuple('PreviewRender',
                                 ['wrapped', 'raw_tail_offset', 'wrapped_tail_offset'])
      ```

      Eager invalidation hooks (drop `preview_render` to None on any of):
        * `set_preview(id, text)` — reset render
        * `clear_preview(id)` / `invalidate_preview(id)` — drop both fields
        * Terminal resize — walk loaded Items, clear `preview_render`
        * `_toggle_preview_ansi` — same
        * `update_data` mod/upsert touching an Item — drop both fields

      Lazy fill at render: `render_preview` reads `item.preview_render`; on `None`, generate by running `_sanitize_preview` + per-line `_wrap_preview_line` over `item.preview`, store on Item, use. On width/ansi mismatch (defensive — eager invalidation should have dropped already), regenerate.

      `append_preview` for this subticket: just invalidates `preview_render` (next paint regenerates). In-place extension is the next subticket.

      Item equality / hashability: ensure `preview` and `preview_render` are excluded from `__eq__` / `__hash__` if those exist; otherwise mutations break dict/set semantics.

      * ## Comments {#422:comments}

        * Commit 1 landed: pure refactor moving preview text from State._preview dict onto Item.preview. All 1793 tests passing. Starting commit 2: wrap cache. {#422:comment:426}

        * Commit 2 landed: Item.preview_render wrap cache with all eager invalidation hooks (set/append/clear/invalidate_preview, terminal resize, preview_ansi toggle, update_data mod/upsert). Defensive width/ansi mismatch check. 14 new unit tests in test/unit/test_preview_render_cache.py. Full suite: 1807 tests, all passing. {#422:comment:427}

    * ## Ticket: Framework: in-place wrap extension on append_preview {#423}

          status: done
          created: 2026-05-21 09:58:07 UTC
          updated: 2026-05-21 11:00:01 UTC

      Optimization on top of the previous subticket. `append_preview(id, chunk)` no longer invalidates the wrap; it extends in place using the tail offsets.

      Algorithm:
        1. `raw_tail_text = item.preview[raw_tail_offset:] + chunk`
        2. Split `raw_tail_text` on `\n` → list of raw lines (last may be partial)
        3. Wrap each new raw line via `_wrap_preview_line`
        4. Replace `wrapped[wrapped_tail_offset:]` with the flattened wrap
        5. Update offsets:
           * new `raw_tail_offset` = position after last `\n` in updated `item.preview` (or `len(preview)` if no newline yet)
           * new `wrapped_tail_offset` = index where the last raw line's wrap starts

      Tests:
        * Append a chunk with no newlines → last partial line extends; wrapped count may grow if width exceeded.
        * Append a chunk with one newline → last partial closes, new partial starts.
        * Append a chunk with multiple newlines → multiple new wrapped lines.
        * Append a very long chunk that wraps multiple times → correct row count.
        * Append after a width change (eager invalidation already dropped render) → next paint regens fresh; subsequent append extends correctly.

      Depends on: previous subticket.

      * ## Comments {#423:comments}

        * Implementation: added _extend_or_drop_preview_render helper in 040-state.py; fixed render_preview's lazy-fill to record correct raw_tail_offset (position after last newline) and wrapped_tail_offset (where last raw line's wrap starts). Added 17 new tests including a property test that splits a fixed text at many positions and verifies incremental == fresh byte-for-byte. Full test suite: 1824 passing (was 1807). {#423:comment:428}

    * ## Ticket: browse-claude: route composer through cached_children + eager-push children + per-record preview on Item {#424}

          status: done
          created: 2026-05-21 09:58:07 UTC
          updated: 2026-05-21 11:14:42 UTC

      Recipe-side unification. All work in `recipes/browse-claude`.

      **Eager-push:** in `_collect_umbrella_preview`, after determining the umbrella's children, push them to the framework via `_BROWSER.update_data(upsert ops)` if not already present. Recursion into nested `#tool:` / `#span:` / `#prompt:` umbrellas also pushes their descendants. One batched `update_data` call per top-level composer invocation.

      **Cache-driven reads:** the composer reads children from `_BROWSER.cached_children(umbrella_id)`. After eager-push, the cache is populated, so recursive descent reuses the framework's data — no duplicate `get_children` calls (subsumes the old #413 goal).

      **Per-record preview cache on Item:** for each leaf child, the composer:
        * Reads `child.preview` — cache hit, append to parts.
        * On miss, calls `_render_record_with_rule(path, n)`, writes back via `_BROWSER.set_preview(child.id, rendered)`, appends to parts.

      The umbrella's own composed preview also goes through `set_preview(umbrella.id, composed)` so the framework caches it on the umbrella's Item too.

      Side effects already audited (see #410 body):
        * Children-grid pane populates for preview-touched umbrellas — positive UX change.
        * `cached_parents()` returns more entries.
        * Memory grows monotonically with preview navigation (bounded by data size).

      Tests:
        * Composer doesn't double-call `get_children` after first invocation.
        * `child.preview` is populated after umbrella's preview is composed.
        * Tail-tick on an umbrella only re-renders the new records (existing children preserve their cached preview).
        * Collapse + re-expand uses cached children (instant).

      Depends on: the two framework subtickets above.

      * ## Comments {#424:comments}

        * Implemented: routed _collect_umbrella_preview through _BROWSER.cached_children, accumulated upserts for eager-push via one batched update_data per top-level call, and added per-leaf preview caching via a batched main-thread post (NOT set_preview — single-slot would lose all but one write). Used _BROWSER.get_cached_preview for the read side. Added 6 new tests covering: graceful no-_BROWSER fallback, no duplicate get_children, leaf.preview population, single update_data per invocation, tail-tick re-renders only new records, collapse + re-expand reuses cache. All 1830 tests pass (one flaky tmux suspend test reran clean). Manual smoke test launched recipe to b.run() initialization without errors. {#424:comment:429}

    * ## Ticket: browse-claude: records as Item extras, shrink _TREE_CACHE (FUTURE) {#425}

          status: future
          created: 2026-05-21 09:58:07 UTC
          updated: 2026-05-21 09:58:16 UTC

      Optimization / cleanup. Optional after the above three subtickets land.

      Recipe attaches the raw JSON record to each Item via custom-attr extras (`upsert(... record=raw_obj)`). `_render_record_with_rule` reads `item.record` directly instead of `_TREE_CACHE.records[n]`.

      `_TREE_CACHE` retains the indexes (`turn_direct`, `tool_children`, `agent_link`, `tool_to_turn_root_line`, `line_offsets`, `assistant_has_tool_use`, etc.) and live-tail byte-offset state — those are computed projections / file-level metadata that don't fit on individual Items. But records themselves move to Items.

      Live-tail `update_data` `mod` ops must update `item.record` when the underlying record mutates (rare but possible — e.g., streaming assistant message updates).

      Mark as future. Land only if the per-record Item.preview path shows real indirection cost we want to eliminate.

    * ## Ticket: Task: Document preview / update_data registration constraints + remove dead preview search-query support {#430}

          updated: 2026-05-21 23:33:05 UTC
          status: done
          created: 2026-05-21 23:22:12 UTC

      Background: #422 moved preview cache onto `Item.preview`, which implicitly added a new contract — `set_preview` / `append_preview` for an id whose Item is not in `_items_by_id` silently drop the text on the floor. Combined with the long-standing rule that `_state._children[parent]` is treated as authoritative once non-None, recipes have two registration constraints they must honour but no explicit documentation about either. This ticket adds the documentation and clears one piece of dead code.

      ## Part A — Documentation

      ### A1. `Browser.update_data` docstring + `Browser.cached_children` docstring + `docs/recipes.md`

      Add a paragraph along these lines (paraphrase as fits the existing voice):

      > **Children-list authority.** Once `_state._children[parent]` is non-None — populated by `get_children` delivery or any `update_data` upsert — the framework treats whatever's there as the parent's children list. There's no "loading more" indicator after the initial population. Tree expansion shows exactly what's in the list at paint time.
      >
      > **Implication:** if you push children for a parent via `update_data(upsert(...))`, you must *eventually* push all siblings. Partial lists are valid as transient states (the tail-worker pattern streams new children over time, and the user sees them appear as they arrive), but a permanently-incomplete list means tree expansion permanently hides the missing siblings. The framework cannot tell "still streaming" from "forgot to push the rest" — that's a recipe-author responsibility.

      ### A2. The four preview-API docstrings (`set_preview` / `append_preview` / `clear_preview` / `invalidate_preview`) + `docs/recipes.md`

      Add a paragraph along these lines:

      > **Registration prerequisite.** These operations no-op when the id is not present in `_items_by_id`. Preview storage lives on the Item (`Item.preview` / `Item.preview_render`), so without a registered Item there's nowhere to write. To cache preview text for an id, ensure the Item is registered first.
      >
      > The cheapest way to ensure an Item exists is an idempotent upsert with no field changes:
      >
      > ```python
      > b.update_data([upsert(id_, parent_id)])
      > b.set_preview(id_, text)
      > ```
      >
      > For an existing id this is patch-merge-with-no-fields (no-op). For a missing id this creates a minimal Item under the given parent; default field values apply (`title=''`, `tag=''`, `has_children=False`, etc.) unless you pass them explicitly. Pair this with the children-list authority rule (A1) — registering one item via upsert puts it in the parent's children list, so you must eventually push the full sibling set under that parent.

      ### A3. `docs/recipes.md`

      Add a short framework-side note:

      > **The framework registers cursor-reachable Items.** `visible_items` synthesizes and registers a scope_root Item when one doesn't already exist (see 040-state.py around the `state.scope_stack` branch), so the per-Item preview cache always has somewhere to land for the cursor's current row. Recipes only need to enforce the registration constraint (A2) for their own pushes — not for cursor navigation.

      ## Part B — Tests

      Add a test class to `test/unit/test_preview_render_cache.py` (or new file if cleaner). Cover:

      * `set_preview(unregistered_id, text)` is a no-op: `get_cached_preview(id)` returns `None`, no Item created.
      * `set_preview(registered_id, text)` writes: `get_cached_preview(id) == text`, `item.preview == text`.
      * `append_preview(unregistered_id, chunk)` is a no-op: same observable as above (Item stays absent or unmodified).
      * `clear_preview(unregistered_id)` is a no-op (doesn't raise).
      * `invalidate_preview(unregistered_id)` is a no-op (doesn't raise).
      * Idempotent-ensure pattern: `update_data([upsert(unknown_id, parent_id)])` then `set_preview(unknown_id, text)` works — Item exists with default fields, preview is cached.
      * Idempotent-ensure on an existing id: `update_data([upsert(existing_id, existing_parent)])` is a no-op — existing fields are not overwritten.

      ## Part C — Code cleanup: remove dead search-query handling in `render_preview`

      Background: `_write_highlighted` (the function that actually draws yellow/bold search highlight overlay) is only called from `render_list`, never from `render_preview`. The `query` / `drop_sgr` branch in `render_preview` (around 050-render.py:1567, 1572-1581) strips SGR for query-matching lines but doesn't apply any highlight overlay afterwards — visually a regression for matching lines (they lose their colors), not a feature. The branch is also the only reason the #422 wrap cache has a "not query" guard.

      Changes in `src-tui/050-render.py`:

      * Remove the `query = getattr(browser, '_search_query', '')` line in `render_preview`.
      * Remove the per-line `drop_sgr` check (and the surrounding comment block about search highlight).
      * Always pass `drop_sgr=False` to `_wrap_preview_line` from `render_preview`.
      * Simplify the wrap-cache enable condition: remove the `not query` clause — the cache is now always candidate-for-use when geometry + ANSI policy match (the existing `_error_text` / `_help_mode` guards stay).
      * `_write_highlighted` and its usage in `render_list` are unchanged — search highlight in the list pane still works.

      Verify by running `./run-tests.sh` — no list-pane tests should regress, and the existing preview tests should still pass.

      ## Out of scope (for future tickets, do not implement here)

      * Adding a `complete` flag to track "this parent's children list is fully populated" — deferred per the design discussion. Reason: would force browse-claude into double-work (composer pushes complete set today, framework would re-fetch on expand unless recipe opts in via `complete_for=...`). Ordering of merged-in children also opens design questions. Revisit only if a real consumer needs true partial-push for tree children.
      * Auto-synthesizing an Item from `set_preview(unknown_id, text)` — explicitly NOT implemented. The contract is "register first" per A2; magical forgiveness would muddy the data model.

    * ## Ticket: Task: Move set_preview to the post queue; preserve single-flight worker {#431}

          updated: 2026-05-22 00:00:18 UTC
          status: done
          created: 2026-05-21 23:47:13 UTC

      Background: `set_preview` is the only preview-write API that doesn't go through the post queue. Today it writes directly to the single-slot `_preview_result` — same slot the worker uses for its own `get_preview` → main-thread handoff. The "latest-wins" semantic was correct for the worker (a cursor-move pivots to the newer request, older results should drop), but it's wrong for recipes — a recipe that calls `set_preview` twice in quick succession loses the first write silently.

      Browse-claude's #424 worked around this by rolling its own `b.post(lambda: ...)` callback for the per-leaf cache. After this ticket, that workaround becomes unnecessary — `set_preview` can be called per leaf and all writes land.

      ## Part A — Recipe-facing `set_preview` goes through the post queue

      In `src-tui/040-state.py`, change `set_preview(id_, text)` to:

      ```python
      def set_preview(self, id_, text) -> None:
          """(thread-safe) Cache preview text for ``id_``.

          Posts a main-thread closure that writes ``item.preview = text`` and
          drops the wrap cache. Multiple calls accumulate via the post queue
          — every write lands.

          No-op when ``id_`` is not in ``_items_by_id`` (see registration
          prerequisite documented under ``cached_preview``).
          """
          if text is None:
              text = ''
          def _apply():
              item = self._state._items_by_id.get(id_)
              if item is not None:
                  item.preview = text
                  item.preview_render = None
              self._needs_redraw.add('preview')
          self.post(_apply)
      ```

      Update the docstring to drop the old "Latest-wins" / "construct with `get_preview=None`" advisory — both go away once the writes are queued.

      **Do NOT change the worker's path.** The worker thread continues to write its `get_preview` result into `_preview_result = (req_id, text)` for the main thread's `apply_preview_result` to consume. That single-slot lane is correct for the worker — it implements the cursor-move latest-wins pivot. Only the recipe-facing `set_preview` API is changing.

      ## Part B — Single-flight worker invariant (verify; don't add new mechanism)

      The framework MUST process at most one `get_preview` fetch at a time. This is already true today via the `_preview_req` single-slot and the worker's main loop pattern. After this change, that invariant must still hold:

      * `request_preview(id_)` writes `_preview_req = id_` directly. Rapid cursor movement just overwrites the slot — newer cursor positions supersede older ones.
      * The worker reads `_preview_req`, fires `get_preview(req_id)`, and on return checks whether `_preview_req` still equals `req_id`. If not, the result is discarded and the worker loops to serve the newer request.
      * For generator `get_preview`, the worker checks `_preview_req != item_id` between yields and abandons (closes the generator) on mismatch.
      * At-most-one in-flight `get_preview` at any moment. Earlier fetches that haven't returned yet block the next one until they complete, but their results are dropped if superseded.

      Implementation requirement: do NOT add concurrent fetches, fetch queues, or parallel worker threads. The single-slot `_preview_req` model is the constraint. If during implementation it looks like a refactor would change this, stop and revisit the design.

      ## Part C — Browse-claude #424 cleanup (drop the manual post workaround)

      In `recipes/browse-claude`:

      * `_preview_umbrella` currently posts a manual `_apply_leaf_previews(b, lp)` callback to write each leaf's preview. Replace with direct `b.set_preview(cid, text)` calls in a loop — each call queues its own closure.
      * Remove the `_apply_leaf_previews` helper if no other caller remains.
      * Remove the `leaf_previews` dict accumulator and the docstring paragraph explaining "set_preview is single-slot, we work around with post".

      Net effect: simpler recipe code, fewer indirections, identical end state.

      ## Part D — Tests

      Add tests under `test/unit/test_preview_render_cache.py` (or a new file):

      1. **Multiple `set_preview` calls all land:**
         - Set up Browser with three Items A, B, C in `_items_by_id`.
         - Call `set_preview(A, 'a-text')`, `set_preview(B, 'b-text')`, `set_preview(C, 'c-text')` in sequence.
         - Drain via `run_until_idle`.
         - Assert all three `item.preview` fields are set correctly. Today's behavior (single-slot) would only keep the last one.

      2. **Ordering with `update_data`:**
         - `update_data([upsert(new_id, parent_id)])`, then `set_preview(new_id, text)`.
         - Drain.
         - Assert new Item exists with cached preview text. Today this works through the slot mechanism too, but the post-queue path makes it explicit FIFO.

      3. **Single-flight worker invariant:**
         - Mock `get_preview` with a callable that:
           - Increments a `currently_fetching` counter on entry, decrements on exit.
           - Records the max value of `currently_fetching` observed.
           - Sleeps briefly (10ms) to give the test time to fire more requests.
           - Returns a string.
         - Fire 20 rapid `request_preview(id)` calls with different ids (all registered).
         - Drain via `run_until_idle`.
         - Assert: `max_currently_fetching == 1` (single-flight invariant).
         - Assert: total `get_preview` calls << 20 (most are superseded before the worker reaches them).

      4. **Worker-recipe race semantics unchanged:**
         - Document and assert the existing rule: if both worker and recipe write previews "around the same time", post queue drains first then `apply_preview_result` consumes the worker slot. Worker wins. Same behavior as before the change — recipes that want guarantees still use `get_preview=None`.

      ## Critical implementation notes

      * Test loader wiring: if any test sets up a minimal Browser without `post`, ensure `post` is wired up. Look at existing tests for the pattern.
      * The post-queue closure captures `id_` by name — make sure the closure binds it correctly (no late-binding bugs in loops if anyone constructs `set_preview` calls in a comprehension elsewhere).
      * `_needs_redraw.add('preview')` continues to fire from within the closure so the renderer picks up the new text on the next pass.
      * Browse-claude's `_collect_umbrella_preview` was passing `leaf_previews` through the recursive descent — when removing that, double-check no other recipe code relies on the dict being assembled before posting.

      ## Out of scope (do not implement)

      * Cancelling an in-flight worker fetch when `set_preview` writes for the same id. Possible future work but adds coordination complexity; current behavior (worker overwrites recipe) is documented and acceptable for the `get_preview=None` recipe pattern.
      * Per-id sequencing guarantees beyond FIFO of the post queue.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cache rendered preview text on Item {#411}

        status: duplicate
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 09:55:40 UTC

    Symptom: in browse-claude, expanding a 496-child umbrella runs `_render_record_with_rule(path, n)` for every child (read JSON record + classify + render). ~350ms total per call; repeated 2-3x per expand due to duplicate composer calls + tail-tick recompose.

    Design (per user direction): store the rendered preview text directly on the Item rather than in the per-id `_state._preview` dict.

    Implications:
      * Leaf items (individual records) cache the output of `_render_record_with_rule` and never re-render unless the underlying record changes.
      * Invalidation is natural: when the framework or recipe mutates an Item (via `update_data` mod/upsert), drop that Item's cached preview.
      * Lifetime tracking is automatic — preview cache dies with the Item; no orphan entries in a sidecar dict.

    Open design questions for this ticket:
      * Should `Item.preview` be opaque text or a structured handle (raw + wrapped form from sibling subticket on wrap cache)?
      * Recipes today populate the preview via `set_preview(id, text)` and `get_preview(item_id)`. Should that stay the entry point with framework writing through to `Item.preview`, or do recipes mutate `Item.preview` directly?
      * Memory footprint: keeping rendered text on every loaded Item could be large. Consider an LRU bound or "drop on collapse" rule.

    Scope: framework storage change; browse-claude is the immediate consumer. Pattern reusable by every recipe whose preview is a deterministic function of the item.

    * ## Comments {#411:comments}

      * Merged into #410. See design discussion 2026-05-21: preview-on-Item with eager invalidation is the same goal as this ticket. {#411:comment:419}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Umbrella preview composition uses cached children-previews {#412}

        status: duplicate
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 09:55:41 UTC

    Symptom: `_collect_umbrella_preview` (recipes/browse-claude:3773) recursively re-renders every descendant on every preview call.

    Design (per user direction): once `Item.preview` caching lands (sibling subticket), umbrella composition becomes "concatenate children's `.preview` fields". On miss, fall through to per-record rendering and write back to the child's `.preview` so it's cached for next time.

    The umbrella's own preview is itself a composition of children's previews and is cacheable on the umbrella's Item via the same mechanism — recursive caching. Invalidation propagates: when a child's preview is invalidated, the umbrella's preview is too.

    Scope: browse-claude. May need a framework primitive ("this Item's preview is the concatenation of its children's previews") if other recipes want to opt into the same pattern. Decide during implementation whether that primitive is worth extracting.

    Depends on: the per-Item preview cache subticket landing first.

    * ## Comments {#412:comments}

      * Merged into #410. Per-record render cache lives on Item.preview after eager-push design; recipe-side composition reads child.preview from framework cache. {#412:comment:420}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Route _collect_umbrella_preview through browser.cached_children {#413}

        status: duplicate
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 09:55:41 UTC

    Symptom: `_collect_umbrella_preview` calls `get_children(item_id)` directly, bypassing the framework cache; one of the 3 duplicate get_children fetches per expand.

    Design (per user direction): `_BROWSER` is already a module-level singleton in browse-claude (set in `main()`, used elsewhere for preview-width lookup). The composer can call `_BROWSER.cached_children(item_id)` directly and fall back to `get_children(item_id)` only on cache miss. No need to pass the browser handle through `get_preview`'s signature.

    Impact: small in absolute terms once the per-Item preview cache lands — the duplicate work becomes cheap. Remains a principled cleanup. If we ever support multiple browser instances per recipe, revisit (would need a handle through the call chain instead of a module global).

    Scope: ~10 LOC in browse-claude. No framework changes.

    * ## Comments {#413:comments}

      * Subsumed by #410: composer reads from _BROWSER.cached_children after eager-push during preview composition. {#413:comment:421}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cache _sub_layout result; expose through official API {#414}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-22 00:42:28 UTC

    Symptom: `_sub_layout(children, width, show_ids)` (050-render.py:1068) recomputes `_fmt_child` + `_wrap_entry` for every child on every paint of the grid pane. For 500 children that's 1000+ string ops per paint.

    Design (per user direction): treat `_sub_layout` as a pure function — store its result in instance variables on the Browser; recompute only when one of its inputs `(children list identity, width, show_ids)` changes. Expose the cached layout through an official API method (e.g., `browser.children_grid_layout()`) so call sites (children-grid sizing in `layout_panes`, the renderer itself) read the same memoized object instead of redoing the work.

    Today the layout is computed twice per paint — once in `layout_panes` to size the grid pane, once in `render_children_grid` to draw it. Single shared cache fixes both.

    Scope: framework-level. Touches `040-state.py` (cache slot), `050-render.py` (production + consumption). Universal benefit.

    Note: this is the list-pane analogue of the preview wrap cache subticket. They share "memoize pure-function results on stable input identity" shape; consider shared helper if convenient.

    * ## Comments {#414:comments}

      * Cache wired: ChildrenGridLayout namedtuple in 030-data.py, _children_grid_cache slot + children_grid_layout() API + _invalidate_children_grid_cache() helper on Browser in 040-state.py, invalidation hooks in update_data._apply and apply_children_results, both _layout_for and render_children_grid routed through the API. 5 new tests in test_children_grid.py covering cache hit/miss-on-width/miss-on-show_ids/invalidation-on-update_data/shared-cache-across-paint-paths. Full suite 1854 passes. {#414:comment:433}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Generator-style get_children for big browse-claude umbrellas (FUTURE) {#415}

        status: future
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 02:06:56 UTC

    UX win: expansion of a 500-child node could show first children within ~10ms instead of blocking ~350ms for the full list. Framework already supports generator return from `get_children` (040-state.py:3822) — each yield becomes a separate `update_data` batch.

    Cost: refactor `_list_prompt_children` / `_list_tool_children` / `_list_span_children` in browse-claude to yield items as found rather than returning a list. ~80 LOC. No framework changes needed.

    Tradeoff: amortises perceived latency but does not reduce total work. Mostly addressed by the per-record render cache (each child becomes microseconds to format with cache hit). Revisit only if the Tier-S caches don't make expand feel instant.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Generator-style _collect_umbrella_preview (FUTURE) {#416}

        status: future
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 02:06:56 UTC

    UX win: preview starts rendering top-down within ~10ms; user can begin reading while bottom is still rendering. Framework already supports `get_preview` returning a generator — `_stream_preview_from_generator` (040-state.py:4090) drains chunks via `append_preview` with buffer cap and demand-pull resume on scroll near tail.

    Cost: ~150 LOC refactor + interaction with tail invalidation, cursor-move abandon, demand-pull resume. Non-trivial correctness surface.

    Tradeoff: pure UX win for first-paint; doesn't reduce total work. Mostly addressed by per-record render cache + umbrella composition cache. Mark future.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Append-only preview path on tail tick (FUTURE) {#417}

        status: future
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 02:06:56 UTC

    Today when the tail worker pushes new children to an umbrella, the recipe calls `invalidate_preview(id)` which forces a full recompose on next paint. An append-only delta could instead call `append_preview(id, rendered_new_chunk)` directly, leaving the existing wrapped buffer intact.

    Tradeoff: per-Item preview cache + umbrella composition cache make full recompose cheap — the marginal win from this path is small. Adds complexity (recipe must reliably detect append-only vs insertion/removal/reparent). Revisit if tail-tick latency is felt after Tier-S caches land.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cache _fmt_child result on Item (FUTURE) {#418}

        status: future
        created: 2026-05-21 02:06:39 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-21 02:06:56 UTC

    Marginal win — `_fmt_child` is already microseconds per call. Caching the formatted string on the Item would shave a few ms per paint of a 500-entry grid. Largely subsumed by the `_sub_layout` result cache (memoizes the entire grid build, not just individual entries).

    Skip unless the `_sub_layout` cache somehow doesn't cover the per-paint cost.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Simplify children-grid layout: drop cache + invalidation hooks; eager recompute with non-None init {#434}

        updated: 2026-05-22 01:06:49 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 00:51:54 UTC

    Background: #414 introduced a single-entry cache for `_sub_layout` results with invalidation hooks in `update_data._apply` and `apply_children_results`. Per design discussion: `_sub_layout` is cheap enough to recompute on demand for realistic workloads. The cache + invalidation machinery is more complexity than the perf saving justifies.

    Simplification goals:
      * **No invalidation hooks** in mutation paths — removes the hooks added to `update_data._apply` / `apply_children_results` for the cache.
      * **Always-valid state** — `Browser._children_grid_layout` initialized at Browser construction with reasonable defaults, never `None`. Removes `None` handling at every read site.
      * **Eager recompute on call** — the layout-producing method calls `_sub_layout(...)` every time and stores the fresh result on the Browser. No key comparison, no cache-hit/miss branch.

    ## Implementation

    In `src-tui/040-state.py`:

    * Replace the current `_children_grid_cache = None` slot with `_children_grid_layout` initialized at Browser construction:

      ```python
      # In Browser.__init__:
      self._children_grid_layout = _sub_layout([], 0, 'auto')
      ```

      Pick defaults that produce a valid empty layout (the existing `_sub_layout` returns `(1, cols, [], [])` for empty children, so any width/show_ids works — pick small fixed values like above).

    * Replace `Browser.children_grid_layout(children, width, show_ids)` with eager recompute:

      ```python
      def children_grid_layout(self, children, width, show_ids):
          """Recompute and return the children-grid layout for the given inputs.

          Always recomputes — the layout is cheap enough that caching adds
          more complexity than it saves. The result is stored on
          ``self._children_grid_layout`` so callers can read the last
          computed layout without re-passing inputs.
          """
          self._children_grid_layout = _sub_layout(children, width, show_ids)
          return self._children_grid_layout
      ```

    * Remove `Browser._invalidate_children_grid_cache()` entirely.

    * Remove invalidation calls to that method from `update_data._apply` (or wherever they live) and from `apply_children_results`.

    In `src-tui/050-render.py`:

    * Call sites (`_layout_for` for sizing, `render_children_grid` for drawing) continue calling `browser.children_grid_layout(children, width, show_ids)`. They now recompute on each call rather than sharing a cached result. Both still land on the same fresh layout per paint cycle (each paint runs `_layout_for` and `render_children_grid` once, so the work is 2x per paint — acceptable given `_sub_layout`'s cheapness).

    ## Tests

    Update `test/unit/test_children_grid.py`'s `TestChildrenGridLayoutCache` class:

    * **Drop:** `test_cache_hit_returns_same_layout_on_identical_input` (identity equality no longer holds — each call produces a fresh object).
    * **Drop:** `test_invalidation_on_update_data_upsert` (no invalidation hooks to test).
    * **Drop:** any test asserting shared object identity between `_layout_for` and `render_children_grid` calls.
    * **Keep/adapt:**
      * `test_cache_miss_on_width_change` — keep as a smoke test that different inputs produce different layouts (object-equality test rather than identity).
      * `test_cache_miss_on_show_ids_change` — same shape.
    * **Add:** `test_default_layout_after_init` — assert `browser._children_grid_layout` is a valid `ChildrenGridLayout` immediately after `Browser.__init__` (non-None, has `num_cols`, `slot_rows`, etc.).
    * **Add:** `test_children_grid_layout_recomputes_every_call` — call twice with identical inputs; assert the work was done both times (e.g., monkey-patch `_sub_layout` with a call-counter, assert count==2).

    Rename the test class from `TestChildrenGridLayoutCache` to `TestChildrenGridLayout` (no longer a cache).

    ## Verification

    * `./run-tests.sh` — all tests pass.
    * `./build-tui.sh` — artifact rebuilds cleanly.
    * Visual smoke test (optional): launch any recipe with a parent that has many children, cursor onto it, verify the grid pane shows correctly. Cursor through siblings — layout updates each time.

    ## Critical constraints

    * Don't add a cache back under another name. The simplification is the point.
    * Don't optimise prematurely (e.g., "skip recompute if inputs match"). If perf shows up as a real problem in profiling, we revisit.
    * Edit `src-tui/*.py`, not the generated artifact. Rebuild via `./build-tui.sh`.
    * Use `plan` CLI for tracking, not TodoWrite / TaskCreate.

    ## Recent context

    Recent commits on `main`:
    - `9de9680` — Cache _sub_layout result on Browser; expose as children_grid_layout API (#414 — this ticket reverses parts of it)
    - `fa95570` — plan: close #410 / #414

    All 1854 tests currently passing.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Redesign preview worker: post-queue delivery + dedup via local_id; re-fire on item.preview=None; skip if cached; preserve scroll {#442}

        updated: 2026-05-22 04:32:27 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 04:12:43 UTC

    Fixes "stuck blank preview" during rapid cursor movement with slow `get_preview`. Root cause: `_update_preview_for_cursor` only re-fires `request_preview` on cursor *change* — when something clears `item.preview` while the cursor stays put, the renderer reads `None` and never recovers.

    ## Design

    ### Part A — Worker redesign

    Replace the `_preview_result` slot with post-queue delivery. Worker keeps a `local_id` from the previous fetch and dedups by comparing it to `_preview_req`.

    Pseudocode:

    ```python
    def _preview_worker(self):
        local_id = None
        while not self._stop:
            req = self._preview_req
            if req == local_id or req is None:
                # Already fetched this, or nothing to fetch. Sleep.
                local_id = None
                self._preview_event.clear()
                # Re-read after clear to catch a request_preview that
                # fired in the gap between read and clear.
                req = self._preview_req
                if req is None or req == local_id:
                    self._preview_event.wait()
                continue
            # New work (different id, or same id re-requested after a prior sleep).
            local_id = req
            self._preview_event.clear()  # arm for "next request during fetch"
            try:
                result = self.get_preview(req) if self.get_preview else ''
            except Exception as e:
                result = f'[error] {type(e).__name__}: {e}'
            if inspect.isgenerator(result):
                self._stream_preview_from_generator(req, result)
                # streaming path delivers via append_preview (already in post queue)
            else:
                if result is None:
                    result = ''
                # Capture by value; do NOT close over `req` / `result` directly.
                self.post(lambda id_=req, r=result:
                          self._deliver_preview(id_, r))
                notify_wake()
    ```

    No lock needed — `_preview_req` is single-attribute read/write (GIL-safe), and the clear-then-re-read pattern handles the race window.

    ### Part B — `_deliver_preview` (new main-thread closure)

    Replaces `apply_preview_result`. Caches the preview unconditionally; only flags redraw if the cursor is still showing this id.

    ```python
    def _deliver_preview(self, id_, text):
        item = self._state._items_by_id.get(id_)
        if item is not None:
            item.preview = text if text is not None else ''
            item.preview_render = None
        # Conditional redraw: cursor may have moved during the fetch.
        if id_ == self._preview_cursor_id:
            self._needs_redraw.add('preview')
    ```

    ### Part C — `_update_preview_for_cursor` fixes the stuck-blank

    Two changes:

    1. **Re-fire when `item.preview is None` even if cursor didn't change.** This closes the gap: any mutation that clears the cache while the cursor sits still gets a fresh fetch on the next main-loop iteration.
    2. **Skip `request_preview` when `item.preview is not None`.** Cursor moving to an already-cached item paints from cache without a redundant fetch.

    ```python
    def _update_preview_for_cursor(self):
        ...
        new_id = ...  # resolve from cursor

        if new_id == self._preview_cursor_id:
            # Cursor on same item. Re-fire ONLY if cache is empty.
            if new_id is not None:
                item = self._state._items_by_id.get(new_id)
                if item is not None and item.preview is None:
                    self.request_preview(new_id)
            return

        self._preview_cursor_id = new_id
        self._preview_scroll = 0  # reset scroll on actual cursor change
        if self._help_mode:
            self._help_mode = False
        self._needs_redraw.add('preview')

        if new_id is None:
            self._preview_req = None
            self._preview_resume_event.set()
            return

        item = self._state._items_by_id.get(new_id)
        if item is not None and item.preview is not None:
            # Already cached — no fetch, just redraw from cache.
            return
        self.request_preview(new_id)
    ```

    ### Part D — Preserve scroll on same-cursor refresh

    When the cursor stays on an item and `_deliver_preview` writes new text, the previously-stored `_preview_scroll` must be preserved. The renderer already clamps `_preview_scroll` to `max(0, len(wrapped) - content_lines)` (050-render.py:1599), so if the new preview is shorter than the old scroll position, the scroll is reduced to the new max naturally on the next paint. No code change needed beyond NOT resetting `_preview_scroll = 0` in the same-cursor branch of `_update_preview_for_cursor` (which the Part C version already gets right by early-returning before the scroll reset).

    `_preview_at_tail` semantics stay as-is: tail-pinned views keep snapping to the new bottom when content grows.

    ### Part E — Removals

    * `Browser._preview_result` field — gone.
    * `Browser.apply_preview_result()` method — gone.
    * Main loop's `self.apply_preview_result()` call in `run` (around 040-state.py:4733 and similar in `run_until_idle` at ~3810) — gone.
    * `run_until_idle`'s idle predicate no longer checks `_preview_result is None`.
    * Worker's "latest-wins single-slot" docstring/comment block (around 040-state.py:2166-2204 area) — rewrite to describe new design.

    ## Behavior notes

    * **Latest-wins is preserved.** Rapid cursor movement A→B→C: worker may post (A, a_text) before realizing the user moved on, then loops, sees `_preview_req=C`, fetches C, posts (C, c_text). Both deliveries land via post queue (no overwrite — different from the old single-slot). Items A through Y get their previews cached even if the user moved on. Memory effect: monotonic but bounded by visited items.

    * **Re-request of same id while in-flight is dropped (accepted).** User calls `invalidate_preview(A)` while worker is fetching A. Worker finishes the in-flight (pre-invalidate) fetch, posts (A, a_text_OLD). Worker loops, sees `_preview_req=A == local_id=A`, sleeps. The post-invalidate fresh fetch does not fire. Net: user sees stale-not-blank for that one cycle. **Accepted per design discussion** — refreshing the same preview while it's already in-flight is rare, and the user can navigate away and back to force a refresh.

    * **Scroll position preserved across refreshes** when cursor stays on the same item. Reset only on actual cursor change.

    ## Tests

    Update / add tests in `test/unit/test_state.py`, `test/unit/test_preview_render_cache.py`, `test/async_/test_workers.py`, `test/async_/_helpers.py`.

    **Tests to drop / rewrite:**
    * Anything that touches `apply_preview_result()` directly — replace with `drain_main_queue()`.
    * Anything that asserts on `_preview_result` slot value — the slot is gone.
    * `TestPreviewWorkerSingleFlight` (from #431) — adapt: still expects single-flight (one `get_preview` in flight at a time), but the assertion mechanism changes (no `_preview_result` to peek at).

    **New tests:**
    1. **Stuck-blank fixed:** simulate cursor on A with `item.preview` already cached. Mutate state to clear `item.preview = None`. Run one main-loop tick (just `_update_preview_for_cursor`). Assert `request_preview` was called for A (or `_preview_req == 'A'`).
    2. **Skip if cached:** cursor moves from A (cached) to B (cached). Assert no `request_preview` fires. (Mock `get_preview` counter == 0.)
    3. **Refresh preserves scroll:** cursor on A. Scroll to row 10. Clear `item.preview`. Drain — fresh fetch, delivery writes new text. Assert `_preview_scroll == 10` (or clamped to max if new text is shorter).
    4. **Scroll resets on cursor change:** cursor on A scrolled to row 10. Move cursor to B. Assert `_preview_scroll == 0`.
    5. **Latest-wins via post queue:** fire `request_preview` for A, B, C in sequence with a slow `get_preview` mock. Drain. Assert items A through C all have `item.preview` written (the in-flight A fetch's result lands too — different from old slot-overwrite behavior).
    6. **Conditional redraw:** worker delivers for id X while cursor is on Y. Assert `_needs_redraw` does NOT add 'preview' (because cursor isn't on X). Cursor moves to X. Assert redraw flagged (via `_update_preview_for_cursor`).
    7. **Single-flight invariant preserved:** as in #431's `TestPreviewWorkerSingleFlight`, fire 20 rapid `request_preview` calls with a mock that tracks `max_in_flight`. Assert `max_in_flight == 1`.

    ## Out of scope

    * Generation-counter / version-tagging for `_preview_req` (alternative fix for the "re-request while in-flight" corner case). Deferred — accept stale-not-blank for now.
    * `_apply_upsert` / `_apply_mod` auto-refetch on cursor item mutation. The Part C `_update_preview_for_cursor` re-fire on `item.preview is None` makes this unnecessary at the framework layer (mutations clear preview → next main-loop iteration re-fires).
    * Generator preview handling changes — the `_stream_preview_from_generator` path stays intact (delivers via `append_preview`, which is already post-queue). Just remove any references to the dead `_preview_result` slot from its comments.

    ## Critical constraints

    * Edit `src-tui/*.py`, not the generated artifact. Rebuild via `./build-tui.sh`.
    * Use the `plan` CLI for tracking.
    * No `--no-verify`, `--amend`, or destructive git operations.
    * One commit covering the redesign is fine. Split into parts if there's a natural seam.

    ## Recent context

    Recent commits on `main`:
    - `1528948` — Move preview cache from state dict to Item.preview
    - `aac2740` — Add Item.preview_render wrap cache with eager invalidation
    - `4779c18` — append_preview: extend wrap cache in place using tail offsets
    - `1b76bb7` — browse-claude: route composer through cached_children + eager-push leaves + per-leaf preview cache
    - `e962b20` — visible_items: register synthesized scope_root in _items_by_id
    - `fc1ea8d` — Document push-API registration constraints; remove dead preview search-SGR branch
    - `78beec3` — set_preview: route through the FIFO post queue (was single-slot)
    - `9de9680` — Cache _sub_layout result on Browser; expose as children_grid_layout API
    - `d0ed5c4` — Drop children-grid layout cache; eager recompute with non-None init

    All 1852 tests passing pre-change.

    * ## Comments {#442:comments}

      * Implemented Parts A-E. Worker now uses local_id dedup + FIFO post-queue delivery via _deliver_preview. _update_preview_for_cursor re-fires when item.preview is None and skips when cached. _preview_result and apply_preview_result removed. 7 new tests in test/async_/test_workers.py (TestPreviewWorkerRedesign442).   * ## Ticket: Task: Attachment foundation: 3 new sub-types, file path-only, _is_voice explicit {#436}

        updated: 2026-05-22 01:33:10 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 00:59:37 UTC

  The recipe already classifies `attachment` records via `_classify` →
  `_render_attachment` and dispatches sub-types through
  `_ATTACH_FORMATTERS`. Three sub-types observed in the wild are missing:

  * `edited_text_file` (shape: `{filename, snippet}`)

  * `compact_file_reference` (shape: `{filename, displayPath}`)

  Plus two adjustments:

  * `_fmt_attach_file` currently expands the file's content into the
    preview pane. Per user feedback: drop the body. Files referenced
    by attachments can be megabytes and reading them is what $EDITOR
    is for. Surface path only.
  * `_is_voice(rec)` returns False for `type == 'attachment'`
    records — explicit branch (today the predicate's `t not in
    ('user', 'assistant')` already excludes them, but the explicit
    branch documents the intent and protects against future
    predicate edits).

  Changes:

  * Add `_fmt_attach_edited_text_file(a)`, `_fmt_attach_plan_mode_exit(a)`,
    `_fmt_attach_compact_file_reference(a)`. Register all three in
    `_ATTACH_FORMATTERS`.
  * Strip the `_extract_attach_file_text` body-expansion from
    `_fmt_attach_file`; delete the helper if no other call site.
  * Add row-title oneliners to the `_summarise_message` attachment
    branch for the three new sub-types.
  * `_is_voice` gains `if t == 'attachment': return False`.

  Tests:

  * New renderer tests for each new sub-type.
  * Update existing `test_file_*` tests — file render is now
    path-only.
  * No body expansion for `file` attachments.
  * `_is_voice` returns False for an `attachment` record (regression).

  * ## Ticket: Task: Orphan subagents in tree view {#437}

        updated: 2026-05-22 01:45:32 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 00:59:37 UTC

  In flat mode, `_list_session_children(jsonl_path)` returns
  `subs + msgs` — every subagent file in `<session>/subagents/` appears
  at the top. In tree mode the same list is returned, but matched
  subagents are *also* rendered inline under their dispatching
  assistant turn (via `td.agent_link` / `agent_to_assistant_line`). So
  in tree mode the duplicate at the top is undesirable, and historically
  the lister has been trimmed to "no top-level subs in tree mode" — but
  that drops orphans (subagent files whose dispatch site is missing
  from the main thread) entirely.

  Fix: split the path.

  * `_list_session_flat(jsonl_path)` — all subs at top + flat messages.
  * `_list_session_tree(jsonl_path)` — orphans only at top + tree messages.

  Routing in `get_children` picks one based on `_TREE_MODE`.

  Orphan computation:

  ```python
  on_disk = {item.agent_id for item in _list_subagents_for_session(jsonl_path)}
  linked  = {info['agent_id'] for info in td.agent_link.values()}
  orphans = on_disk - linked
  ```

  Orphan items get a distinguishing tag style — dim, with `orphan` in
  the tag suffix so the user can see they're not wired:

  ```python
  item.tag = f'{agent_type} · {count} msg · orphan · {_human_time(mtime)}'
  item.tag_style = 'dim'
  ```

  Tests (unit + UI):

  * Unit: fixture with 3 subagent files where 2 have matching
    dispatches → tree-mode lister returns 1 orphan sub + N messages;
    flat-mode lister returns all 3 subs + N messages.
  * UI: open a session with an orphan subagent in tree mode; assert
    the orphan appears at the top of the list with `orphan` in its
    tag.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Tool-result fallback + sourceToolAssistantUUID pairing {#438}

        updated: 2026-05-22 01:48:11 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 00:59:37 UTC

  `toolUseResult` is absent in subagent jsonls (verified across multiple
  samples). The recipe's tool-result formatters key on top-level
  `obj.toolUseResult` and produce empty bodies for subagent records.

  Two changes:

  **1. Tool-result extraction with fallback.**

  Add a helper:

  ```python
  def _extract_tool_result(rec):
      """Return a uniform {tool_use_id, content, is_error} dict, or None.

      Prefers top-level ``rec.toolUseResult`` (main-thread shape); falls
      back to the inline ``message.content[].content`` block when
      ``type == 'tool_result'`` (subagent shape).
      """
  ```

  Update `_fmt_tur_*` formatters and `get_preview` paths that today
  read `obj.toolUseResult` directly to go through `_extract_tool_result`
  instead. Single source of truth.

  Care: the main-thread `toolUseResult` shape carries richer fields
  (`status`, `agentId`, `agentType`, `totalDurationMs`, `usage`,
  `toolStats`). Those only appear on main-thread records, so the
  formatters that key on them stay specific to that shape. Only the
  basic `{tool_use_id, content, is_error}` shape goes through the
  fallback.

  **2. `sourceToolAssistantUUID` pairing.**

  `_resolve_tool_owner` today checks (in order):
  * `message.content[].tool_use_id` against `tool_owner` map
  * `attachment.toolUseID` against `tool_owner` map
  * `rec.sourceToolUseID` against `tool_owner` map

  Add `rec.sourceToolAssistantUUID` — its value is an assistant UUID,
  not a tool_use id, so when present it resolves directly against
  `td.line_of` / `td.by_uuid`. Integrate so it's a stronger signal
  when present.

  Tests:

  * `_extract_tool_result` returns the inline block when
    `toolUseResult` is missing; returns the top-level shape when
    present.
  * Subagent record with no `toolUseResult` renders a non-empty
    tool-result body in the preview.
  * `_resolve_tool_owner` picks up a record whose only back-pointer
    is `sourceToolAssistantUUID`.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Scope card on synthetic top row {#439}

  ── browse-claude
     path:        <abs path>
     sessionId:   <uuid>
     entrypoint:  cli
     cwd:         /…
     gitBranch:   main

     lines:       1591

  ── browse-claude (subagent)
     path:        <abs path>

  sessionId / cwd / gitBranch / entrypoint / slug (all stamped on
  every record); `_TreeData` already has line counts; mtime from
  stat; voice count via `sum(_is_voice(r) for r in td.records)`,
  computed lazily and cached on `td` as `td.voice_count`.

  For agentId / agentType / description on subagent files: the
  filename gives agentId; `agent-<agentId>.meta.json` provides
  agentType + description. The recipe already has
  `_read_subagent_meta` for this.

  Implementation:

  * New `_fmt_scope_card(path, td)` helper.
  * `_preview_umbrella` for the bare-path id prepends the card,
    followed by a rule, followed by the cascade body.
  * `td.voice_count` cached lazily so repeated previews don't
    re-walk records.

  Defensive: if the file is not a Claude jsonl (no sessionId stamps),
  card omits Claude-specific fields and shows path + lines + mtime.

  Tests:

  * Every Claude session field present when source records carry
    them.
  * Missing `slug` omitted gracefully.
  * Subagent variant renders agentId/agentType/description.
  * Non-Claude jsonl renders minimal card without crashing.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Cross-file file-name header + subagent-umbrella-as-voice cleanup {#440}

        updated: 2026-05-22 01:55:25 UTC
        status: done
        created: 2026-05-22 00:59:37 UTC

  **Cross-file header.** When the user navigates to a subagent
  umbrella (id contains `#agent:`), its preview is composed from its
  own jsonl. Prepend a single line at the top:

  ```
  ── file: agent-<agentId>.jsonl ──
  ```

  Implemented in `_preview_umbrella` (the public entry-point of the
  cascade): detect a cross-file id and prepend the header before
  invoking the recursive descent.

  Use a helper `_resolve_file_for_umbrella(id) -> path` so the rule
  generalises if/when other cross-file umbrellas appear (e.g.,
  `compact_file_reference` items linking to a prior session file).

  **Subagent-umbrella-as-voice cleanup.** `_passes_filter` today has a
  hardcoded `if suffix.startswith('agent:'): return True` override.
  Reroute through `_is_voice` so the predicate is uniform:

  * The subagent umbrella row in the parent file is built from a
    voice anchor (the dispatching `Agent` `tool_use` row). Set its
    `kind = 'subagent'` and have `_is_voice` recognise that kind as
    voice. Behaviorally identical to today (still always visible
    under filter) — just cleaner predicate semantics.

  **Compact stub removal.** `_collect_umbrella_preview` today emits a
  compact "subagent" stub line for `#agent:` children when composing
  the parent's preview. Drop it — the dispatch pair (`Agent`
  tool_use + matching tool_result) already lives in the parent file
  and is rendered through the normal leaf path under the dispatching
  turn, so the stub is duplicative.

  Per spec: parent preview composition does NOT descend into the
  subagent jsonl (cross-file boundary). That continues; only the
  stub disappears.

  Tests:

  * `_preview_umbrella` for a `#agent:` id begins with the file-name
    header line.
  * `_passes_filter` for `#agent:` ids returns True via the voice
    path (regression: still always visible under filter).
  * `_collect_umbrella_preview` for a parent containing a `#agent:`
    child does NOT emit the compact stub line.
