* ## Ticket: Doc-rot: fix two stale docstrings in 040-state.py {#444}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-25 04:12:33 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-25 04:17:46 UTC

  Two docstrings disagree with the current code. Both are local edits.

  ### 1. `Browser.drain_main_queue` (line 3685-3691)

  Current docstring claims:

  > Runs only fns that were already in the queue when we started --
  > callables that post further work end up running on the next
  > drain (so there's no risk of a tight loop monopolising the main
  > thread). queue.Queue's get_nowait gives us the right semantics.

  Implementation is `while True: get_nowait()` until `queue.Empty`, so
  fns posted DURING the drain run on the same drain — the docstring's
  "next drain" claim is false.

  Fix: rewrite the docstring to match actual behaviour ("drains until
  empty; callables that post further work run in the same drain"). The
  tight-loop concern the old text raised is real but addressed
  elsewhere — keep the language conservative.

  ### 2. `Browser` class docstring (line 1892, in particular line 1896)

  Says:

  > the latest-wins preview worker

  Post-#442 the worker's *request slot* is still latest-wins but
  delivery is FIFO through the post queue. Update to something like
  "the preview worker (latest-wins request slot, FIFO delivery via the
  post queue)" so readers don't think delivery races overwrite each
  other.

  ### Verification

  * `./run-tests.sh` (or whatever the standard test entrypoint is) —
    these are docstring-only changes, no behaviour to test, but the
    suite should still pass.
  * Grep for other places that say "latest-wins preview" and update
    if any match — there shouldn't be many.

  * ## Comments {#444:comments}

    * Updated drain_main_queue docstring to describe actual behaviour (drains until empty, fns posted during drain run in same drain). Updated Browser class docstring to say 'preview worker (latest-wins request slot, FIFO delivery via the post queue)'. Re-flowed surrounding lines. Grepped for other 'latest-wins preview' mentions in 040-state.py: only request_preview docstring matches, which is still accurate. All 1891 tests pass. {#444:comment:447}

* ## Ticket: `_apply_upsert`: don't drop preview when fields is empty {#445}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-25 04:12:33 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-25 04:21:55 UTC

  Lines 794-802 of `src-tui/040-state.py`, on the existing-id branch:

  ```python
  for k, v in fields.items():
      setattr(existing, k, v)
  existing.preview = None
  existing.preview_render = None
  ```

  Even a no-fields upsert (used as the documented idempotent-ensure
  before `set_preview`, or just a reposition-via-`where=` call) nukes a
  perfectly good cached preview. The documented `update_data([upsert(id,
  parent)]) + set_preview(id, text)` pattern still works because the
  post queue is FIFO and `set_preview` lands after, but any recipe that
  upserts an existing item *without* immediately following with
  `set_preview` loses the cache for no reason.

  ### Fix

  Cheap gate: only drop the preview when `fields` actually changed
  something. Minimum bar: skip the drop when `fields` is empty. Better:
  skip when no value actually differs from the existing field. Pick
  whichever is cheap to implement — the empty-fields gate alone catches
  the documented idempotent-ensure pattern, which is the common case.

  Apply the same gate to `_apply_set` and `_apply_mod` if they have the
  same unconditional drop (check before editing). The intent is "mutate
  → invalidate", so a no-op patch should not invalidate.

  ### Tests

  * Add a unit test: cache a preview on an existing item, run an
    empty-fields `upsert(id, parent)`, assert `item.preview` is
    unchanged.
  * Add a unit test: cache a preview, run an `upsert` that mutates a
    field, assert the preview cache *is* dropped (current behaviour
    preserved when fields actually change).
  * Verify the documented idempotent-ensure pattern in `set_preview`'s
    docstring still works (likely covered by existing tests).

  ### Verification

  * Run the full test suite.

  * ## Comments {#445:comments}

    * Added empty-fields gate to _apply_upsert and _apply_mod: preview/preview_render only cleared when fields actually present (for mod, after dropping the id key). _apply_set was checked and needs no gate -- it constructs a fresh Item so no cache to invalidate. Added 7 new tests in test_update_data_ops.py: TestUpsertPreviewCacheGate (4 tests covering no-fields, patch-only no-fields, real mutation, custom-attr mutation) and TestModPreviewCacheGate (3 tests covering no-fields, id-only patch, real mutation). Full suite: 1898 tests, all pass. {#445:comment:448}

* ## Ticket: Batch preview-cache mutations: preview ops in `update_data` {#446}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-25 04:12:33 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-25 04:44:56 UTC

  Hot-path optimisation. `_preview_umbrella` in `recipes/browse-claude`
  (line 3677) batches its tree mutations into one `update_data(ops)`
  call, then loops `_BROWSER.set_preview(cid, text)` per leaf — one
  closure + queue.put + pipe write per leaf. For a 1000-message session
  that's 1000 closures and 1000 wake notifications where one would do.

  ### Design (agreed with user)

  Add new op tuples consumed by `apply_ops` so preview mutations live
  on the same batch lane as tree mutations. Existing
  `Browser.set_preview` / `append_preview` / `clear_preview` /
  `invalidate_preview` / `drop_preview_cache` stay as thin wrappers
  that delegate to `update_data([op])` — single-call API unchanged,
  semantics unchanged, batched callers pay closure cost once.

  ### Op vocabulary

  Add to the `apply_ops` switch. Suggested names (op-helper functions
  at module scope; pick names that don't collide with `Browser`
  methods — `set_preview_op` etc., or rename to taste):

  | Op tuple | Effect (matches existing single-call method) |
  |---|---|
  | `('set_preview', id, text)` | `item.preview = text or ''`; drop `preview_render` |
  | `('append_preview', id, chunk)` | rmw on `item.preview`; `_extend_or_drop_preview_render` |
  | `('clear_preview', id)` | `item.preview = None; preview_render = None` |
  | `('invalidate_preview', id)` | clear + `request_preview(id)` |
  | `('drop_preview_cache', id_or_none)` | clear (one or all) + cursor-kick if applicable |

  ### Side-effect plumbing

  `apply_ops` is currently pure state mutation — it takes `state`, no
  `Browser`. Preview ops need to:

  * Mark `_needs_redraw.add('preview')` once if any preview op ran.
  * Call `request_preview(...)` for invalidate / drop ops where
    appropriate.

  Options for the implementer to pick:

  1. Have `apply_ops` populate side-effect fields on `state` (e.g.
     `state._preview_dirty`, `state._pending_preview_kick_id`) and let
     `update_data._apply` translate them to Browser-level actions.
  2. Walk the ops list in `update_data._apply`: tree ops to
     `apply_ops`, preview ops handled inline with `self` in scope.

  Either is fine. `request_preview` is a latest-wins slot setter
  already (idempotent for same id; last id wins for different ids), so
  no batch-level dedupe logic is needed — calling it once per op or
  once at end-of-batch produces the same observable result.

  ### Wrapper refactor

  After ops land, refactor each `Browser` preview method to be:

  ```python
  def set_preview(self, id_, text):
      self.update_data([set_preview_op(id_, text)])
  ```

  Keep the docstrings — the contract doesn't change.

  ### Recipe update

  In `recipes/browse-claude:_preview_umbrella` (line 3677-3730):

  * Drop the trailing `for cid, text in leaf_previews.items(): _BROWSER.set_preview(cid, text)` loop.
  * Extend the `ops` list built by `_collect_umbrella_preview` with
    `set_preview_op(cid, text)` entries for each leaf in
    `leaf_previews`.
  * One `_BROWSER.update_data(ops)` call covers both tree upserts and
    preview cache writes.
  * The FIFO ordering inside one `update_data` batch means the upsert
    that registers a new leaf still lands before the `set_preview` op
    that targets it — the docstring's registration-prerequisite stays
    satisfied.

  ### Tests

  * Unit test each new op: apply via `apply_ops`, assert the resulting
    `Item.preview` / `preview_render` state.
  * Test mixed batches: `[upsert(...), set_preview_op(...)]` applied
    in one `update_data` call → both visible after one drain.
  * Test the `invalidate_preview` and `drop_preview_cache` ops kick
    `request_preview` correctly (likely needs a mock or a flag check
    on `_preview_req`).
  * Existing `_preview_umbrella` tests (in
    `test/unit/test_browse_claude_render.py`) should keep passing
    against the refactored recipe — they verify behaviour, not the
    call count.
  * Existing `set_preview` / `append_preview` / `clear_preview` /
    `invalidate_preview` / `drop_preview_cache` unit tests should
    keep passing against the wrapper refactor.

  ### Out of scope

  * `update_data` itself is already a single post. No change needed to
    the batch entry point.
  * Tree-mutation ops are unchanged.
  * No public API rename — existing methods stay.

  ### Verification

  * Run the full test suite.
  * Open a large browse-claude session interactively (1000+ messages)
    and confirm preview composition still works visually. (Optional —
    benchmark before/after wake count if easy, but not required to
    close the ticket.)

  * ## Comments {#446:comments}

    * Implemented batched preview ops via Option 1 (state-field side-effect plumbing). {#446:comment:449}

      Changes:
      - src-tui/040-state.py: added 5 op constructors (set_preview_op, append_preview_op, clear_preview_op, invalidate_preview_op, drop_preview_cache_op); added _apply_set_preview / _apply_append_preview / _apply_clear_preview / _apply_drop_preview_cache; extended apply_ops to dispatch them; apply_ops now resets and populates state._preview_dirty (bool) and state._preview_kicks (list of ('id', cid) | ('cursor', None) | ('cursor_if', cid)) per batch; apply_ops gains a preview_ansi keyword (default True) forwarded to _extend_or_drop_preview_render for append ops; Browser.update_data._apply reads the side-effect signals and translates to _needs_redraw.add('preview') + request_preview calls; refactored set_preview / append_preview / clear_preview / invalidate_preview / drop_preview_cache into thin wrappers that delegate to update_data([op]).
      - recipes/browse-claude: imports set_preview_op; _preview_umbrella appends set_preview_op entries to the same ops list it built for tree upserts, so one update_data covers both tree mutations and per-leaf preview writes — one closure/wake per umbrella regardless of leaf count.
      - test/unit/test_update_data_ops.py: +49 tests covering each op's state mutation, kick recording, dirty-flag reset semantics, and mixed batches (upsert + set_preview_op together).
      - test/unit/test_preview_cache_api.py: +8 Browser-level tests verifying that batched update_data calls translate preview ops into request_preview kicks and that a mixed batch is delivered through one post-queue closure.
      - test/unit/test_browse_claude_render.py: added set_preview_op stub to browse_tui module stub; extended _FakeBrowser.update_data to interpret set_preview ops.
      Side-effect-plumbing choice: Option 1 (state fields), because the ticket text said 'Add to the apply_ops switch' and it lets apply_ops stay (state, ops)-pure with the Browser-coupling concentrated in update_data._apply.
      Tests: 1898 before -> 1955 after (+57), all green. Binary rebuilt with build-tui.sh.

* ## Ticket: Task: Children prefetch slot — latest-wins single-flight for cursor-driven children fetches {#481}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-27 06:24:21 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-27 07:37:29 UTC

  Implement spec docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-27-children-prefetch-slot-design.md.

  Goal: cursor-driven children prefetch becomes latest-wins, mirroring the preview
  worker's single-slot design. Same children worker thread; slot-first priority over
  the existing FIFO. No new concurrency primitives; recipes unchanged.

  Acceptance:
  * Rapid cursor movement coalesces to ≪ N get_children calls (currently ~N).
  * max in-flight get_children == 1 across both slot and FIFO sources.
  * Existing tests in test/async_/test_workers.py keep passing.
  * New unit tests cover: rapid-coalesce, single-flight, slot-first priority, FIFO
    drain-after-settle, no-dup with concurrent explicit refresh, cache-invalidation
    re-fire.
  * UI test (test/ui/test_recipe_browse_git.py) shows rapid scroll lands the
    children pane within a fixed budget.

  * ## Comments {#481:comments}

    * Implementation complete. Before/after on a 15-keystroke browse-git scroll: get_children dropped from 32 to 5 calls. All 2050 tests green. Spec at docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-27-children-prefetch-slot-design.md. {#481:comment:491}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Stage 3 — Restructure `_children_worker` to two-pass slot-first loop {#484}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 06:24:21 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 06:29:42 UTC

    Replace the existing `while not self._stop: event.wait(); while queue: drain`
    structure with the two-pass loop from the spec's "Worker loop restructure"
    section. Pass 1: drain slot until quiescent (skip cache hits and pending hits).
    Pass 2: drain ONE FIFO entry. Sleep with clear-then-check-then-wait when both
    are quiet; reset `_children_prefetch_local_id = None` on wake from `.wait()`.

    Slot stays unused (still None — Stages 4-5 wire it up). All existing FIFO tests
    must pass unchanged.

    Verify: existing test_workers.py and test_pending.py green.

  * ## Ticket: Stage 5 — Slot write path: `_update_children_for_cursor` writes the slot {#486}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 06:24:21 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 06:35:26 UTC

    Rewrite `_update_children_for_cursor` (040-state.py:6031) per the spec.

    TDD. Write a new test:

        def test_rapid_cursor_moves_coalesce_children_prefetch(self):
            lock = threading.Lock()
            state = {'in_flight': 0, 'max_in_flight': 0, 'total': 0}
            def get_children(id_, *, reload=False):
                with lock:
                    state['in_flight'] += 1
                    state['max_in_flight'] = max(state['max_in_flight'],
                                                  state['in_flight'])
                    state['total'] += 1
                time.sleep(0.01)
                with lock:
                    state['in_flight'] -= 1
                return [(f'{id_}/c',)]
            # Build a flat list of 20 expandable items as children of root.
            items = [(f'p{i}', None, {'has_children': True}) for i in range(20)]
            def root_children(id_, *, reload=False):
                if id_ is None:
                    return [{'id': f'p{i}', 'has_children': True}
                            for i in range(20)]
                return get_children(id_, reload=reload)
            b = make_browser(get_children=root_children, show_children_pane=True)
            try:
                b.refresh()
                b.run_until_idle()
                # Drive 20 cursor moves through visible items 0..19.
                for i in range(20):
                    b._state.cursor = i
                    b._update_children_for_cursor()
                b.run_until_idle()
                self.assertEqual(state['max_in_flight'], 1)
                self.assertLess(state['total'], 20,
                    f'expected coalesce; got {state["total"]} fetches')
                # Last cursor's id MUST be in cache.
                self.assertIn('p19', b._state._children)
            finally:
                b.stop_workers()

    Implement the new `_update_children_for_cursor` body. Confirm the test passes
    and that existing tests still pass.

    TDD. Write the test:

        def test_cache_invalidation_re_kicks_slot(self):
            calls = []
            def get_children(id_, *, reload=False):
                calls.append(id_)
                return [(f'{id_}/c',)]
            b = make_browser(get_children=lambda id_, *, reload=False:
                             [{'id': 'A', 'has_children': True}]
                             if id_ is None else get_children(id_, reload=reload),
                             show_children_pane=True)
            try:
                b.refresh()
                b.run_until_idle()
                b._state.cursor = 0
                b._update_children_for_cursor()
                b.run_until_idle()
                self.assertEqual(calls, ['A'])
                # Clear cache for A. update_data with clear_children op.
                b.update_data([('clear_children', 'A')])
                b.run_until_idle()
                # Cursor still on A — should re-fetch.
                b._update_children_for_cursor()
                b.run_until_idle()
                self.assertEqual(calls, ['A', 'A'])
            finally:
                b.stop_workers()

    Confirm the test passes.

  * ## Ticket: Stage 8 — UI test: browse-git rapid scroll lands children pane within budget {#489}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 06:24:21 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 06:39:54 UTC

    Extend test/ui/test_recipe_browse_git.py with one new test:

        def test_rapid_scroll_children_pane_lands(self):
            with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmp:
                # Use _make_repo extended to 30 commits so j-scroll has room.
                _make_repo_with_n_commits(tmp, n=30)
                with TmuxFixture(cols=120, rows=30) as t:
                    t.send_line(f'cd {tmp}')
                    t.launch(_BIN, '--run-py', _RECIPE)
                    t.wait_for('commit', timeout=5.0)
                    # Burst 25 j's.
                    for _ in range(25):
                        t.send('j')
                    # After cursor stops, the children pane should populate within
                    # ~1s, NOT scale with the burst depth.
                    # Capture the commit message on the cursor row (visible in
                    # list), then assert the children pane shows at least one
                    # file path within budget.
                    deadline = time.monotonic() + 1.5
                    found = False
                    while time.monotonic() < deadline:
                        pane = t.capture()
                        # Children pane shows '<sha>:<path>' rows for files.
                        if ':' in pane and any('.' in seg
                                                for seg in pane.split('\n')):
                            found = True
                            break
                        time.sleep(0.05)
                    self.assertTrue(found,
                        'children pane did not populate within 1.5s '
                        'after rapid scroll')
                    t.send('q')

    Add `_make_repo_with_n_commits(tmp, n)` helper that loops `n` times creating
    a one-line file per commit (faster than per-test setup of an arbitrary repo).

    Verify against `./run-tests.sh`.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Stage 9 — Cursor promotes same-id FIFO entry to front {#492}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 07:10:19 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 07:12:45 UTC

    Bug: when `_update_children_for_cursor` sees `new_id` in
    `_children_pending`, it currently skips the slot write. If the id is
    also in the FIFO queue (added by `_dispatch_children` / refresh /
    expand), the worker drains FIFO in order — so the cursor's children
    end up loading LAST among queued entries.

    Fix: when `new_id` is in pending, scan the FIFO for an entry with
    the same id. If found, remove it from its current position and
    `appendleft` so the worker's Pass 2 drains it first. Preserve the
    `reload` flag from the queued tuple. Slot value also updated to
    reflect the cursor (semantic clarity; idempotent if already there).

    Implementation:
    * Add `self._children_queue_lock = threading.Lock()` in
      `Browser.__init__`. The lock protects multi-step FIFO ops
      (scan + del/remove + appendleft) against the worker's popleft.
      Single-step `.append()` from other dispatch paths stays unlocked
      (GIL-atomic on deque).
    * In `_update_children_for_cursor`, when `new_id in
      state._children_pending`, take the lock, scan the queue, remove
      the matching entry (by value via `.remove()` to be index-shift
      safe), and `appendleft` it. Set the wake event.
    * In `_children_worker` Pass 2, take the lock around the popleft.

    Tests:
    * `test_cursor_promotes_fifo_entry_to_front` — preload FIFO with
      (A, X) via two `b.refresh()` calls; gate `get_children` so A is
      in flight while X is in FIFO. Move cursor onto X. Assert X
      delivers before B in the order list.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Stage 10 — FIFO worker skips fetch when cached and `reload=False` {#493}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 07:10:19 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 07:15:22 UTC

      Symmetry with the slot path: when a FIFO entry comes up for an
      id whose cache is already populated and `reload=False`, the
      worker should skip the `get_children` call but still complete
      the delivery housekeeping so Pendings resolve and
      `_children_pending` clears.

      Implementation: in `_fetch_and_deliver_children`, early-return
      when `not reload_ and id_ in self._state._children`. Still post
      `_post_children_delivery(id_)` and call `notify_wake()` so
      `refresh().then()` chains and `run_until_idle` work.

      Tests:
      * `test_fifo_entry_skips_fetch_when_cached_and_no_reload` —
        pre-populate `state._children['X']`, enqueue ('X', False) +
        mark pending, assert no get_children call but pending discards.
      * `test_fifo_entry_with_reload_true_still_fetches_when_cached` —
        sibling: same setup but reload=True, assert get_children DOES
        fire.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Stage 11 — Worker takes over promotion; remove redundant cache check {#495}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 07:31:58 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 07:37:29 UTC

    Two related corrections from the user:

    1. The slot worker's "skip if `slot_id in _children_pending`" gate is
       incorrect for the priority semantics. When the slot has an id that
       also happens to be in FIFO, the worker should pull the FIFO entry,
       copy its `reload` flag, and fetch via the slot path immediately —
       not defer to FIFO drain. Move the promotion logic from
       `_update_children_for_cursor` (main thread) into the worker's
       Pass 1.

    2. Now that `_fetch_and_deliver_children` shorts on cached `reload=False`
       (Stage 10), the explicit `if slot_id in self._state._children: continue`
       in Pass 1 is duplicate logic — remove it. Helper owns the cache
       check.

    Implementation:
    * Simplify `_update_children_for_cursor`: drop the in-pending FIFO
      promotion branch. Always write slot when not cached. Re-fire path
      stays.
    * Restructure worker Pass 1:
      - Decide `reload_` based on whether `slot_id` is in pending: scan
        FIFO under lock; if found, `.remove()` it and copy the entry's
        `reload`. If pending but not in FIFO, the work is already in
        flight from a previous slot iter — `continue` (local_id will
        catch the loop on next read).
      - Otherwise (fresh): `_children_pending.add(slot_id)` and fetch
        with `reload=False`.
      - Drop the Pass 1 cache short-circuit; helper handles it.
    * Update tests that assumed the main-thread promotion or the old
      pending-skip behavior.

* ## Ticket: Epic: Filter visible-tree-only semantic {#496}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-27 22:31:34 UTC

  Replace the optimistic-keep-visible rule in `_recompute_filter_hidden`
  with a strictly visible-tree DFS, plus per-op propagation hook for
  incremental updates. Fixes the bug where umbrellas without matching
  visible content stay on screen until the cursor moves with preview on
  — the filter was effectively coupled to browse-claude's preview
  generator as its sole materialization side channel.

  Design: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-27-filter-visible-tree-only-design.md

  * ## Ticket: Task: Rewrite _recompute_filter_hidden to walk the visible tree (TDD) {#497}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 22:31:34 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 22:48:11 UTC

    Drop the optimistic `has_children and id not in _children` branch.
    Drop the `state._children.keys()` outer loop and the `visited` set.
    Walk a single DFS rooted at the scope row (when scoped) or
    root_id's children (unscoped). Skip `Item.hidden` items entirely.
    Preserve the scope-row exemption.

    Tests (test/unit/test_filter.py):
    - Collapsed parent: self-match only; children not consulted.
    - Deep match through expanded chain: every expanded ancestor stays
      visible; non-matching siblings hidden.
    - Recipe-hidden row containing a match: excluded; doesn't scaffold.
    - Uncached-children parent: NO LONGER optimistic — if self doesn't
      match and no expanded children match, hidden.
    - Multiple filters: AND semantics unchanged.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Add _propagate_filter_status_up helper (TDD) {#498}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 22:31:34 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 22:56:20 UTC

    Bottom-up walk re-evaluating one item then ancestors until status
    stabilizes. Used by per-op `update_data` dispatch and by `expand`'s
    subtree-revisit. Single function used by every per-item update path.

    Tests (test/unit/test_filter.py):
    - Add matching child to hidden parent: walks up, flips parent.
    - Add non-matcher to scaffold-visible parent: walk terminates at
      parent (early-out, ancestors not touched).
    - Mod-flip last matcher to non-matcher: walks up, hides parent.
    - Remove last matcher in a scaffold: walks up, hides parent.
    - Walk reaches root without status change: terminates cleanly.

    * ## Comments {#498:comments}

Handles recipe-hidden items (skip flag write but continue propagation upward), scope-row exemption applied per-item.   * ## Ticket: Task: Wire per-op propagation in update_data._apply (TDD) {#499}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-27 22:31:34 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-27 23:24:02 UTC

    Replace the existing full-walk hook with per-affected-item
    propagation via `_propagate_filter_status_up`. Skip when the
    affected parent is collapsed or uncached (Rule 2 — invisible
    change). Keep `apply_children_results`'s full walk as the fallback
    for the rare legacy delivery path.

    Tests (test/async_/test_browser.py):

      propagates O(depth); pre-existing items unchanged.

    - Remove op clearing the last matcher: parent flips to hidden.

    * ## Comments {#499:comments}

      * Design choice: Pre-scan ops_list to capture (op_kind, item_id, parent_id, is_new, old_parent_id) tuples BEFORE apply_ops mutates state. Then call apply_ops. Then iterate the dispatch tuples to call _propagate_filter_status_up. Rationale: minimal churn (no apply_ops signature change), captures pre-state cleanly for new-vs-existing detection, separates concerns. Old_parent is captured for reparent cases (item leaves its old parent, propagation should reach the old parent too). {#499:comment:509}

      * Pre-existing flake: test/ui/test_recipe_browse_claude.py::test_tree_right_on_session_jumps_to_latest_turn_root fails when run as part of the full UI suite (159s wall time), but passes when run in isolation OR within only test_recipe_browse_claude.py. Confirmed pre-existing — same failure occurs without my changes. Not blocking #499. {#499:comment:510}

      * Implementation complete. Files changed: src-tui/040-state.py (added _filter_visit_subtree, _filter_dispatch_pre_scan, _is_parent_visible_expanded, _dispatch_filter_propagation; refactored _recompute_filter_hidden to share visit logic; wired update_data._apply to call dispatcher), test/async_/test_browser.py (added TestFilterUpdateDataPerOpDispatch with 4 tests). All 1922 unit+async tests pass; existing TestFilterUpdateDataIntegration test still passes verifying scaffold-parent resurrection on matching child upsert. {#499:comment:511}

* ## Ticket: Task: browse-md — markdown structural browser recipe {#517}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-28 19:51:19 UTC

  New recipe `recipes/browse-md` (~350 lines, single file, executable).
  Spec: `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-28-browse-md-design.md`.

  Lifts md2ansi.py's regex fragments and combined-regex parser shape
  (`_m2a_build_context` technique) for linear, non-recursive parsing
  of one markdown file into a tree of headings + nested list items.
  Preview is a byte-slice of the slurped source; `m` toggles md2ansi
  rendering of the preview; `V`/`E` open source (root → original
  file; non-root → temp file with merged byte ranges); `M` pages
  preview through external md2ansi.

  Acceptance criteria:
  * `recipes/browse-md README.md` opens, shows headings + nested lists.
  * `recipes/browse-md README.md#42` opens scoped into the item that
    contains line 42.
  * `recipes/browse-md README.md#Goals` opens scoped into the first
    heading matching "Goals" (exact → prefix → substring fallback).
  * Cursor on a heading → preview shows that heading and every
    descendant, rendered with md2ansi.
  * `m` toggles between rendered and raw preview.
  * `V` on root pages the original file in `$PAGER`; `V` on non-root
    items pages a temp file with merged/sorted byte ranges.
  * `E` on root edits the original file in place; `E` on non-root
    items opens a temp file (edits discarded).
  * Ctrl-R re-slurps and re-parses the file.

  * ## Comments {#517:comments}

    * All sub-tickets done. Acceptance criteria verified end-to-end: {#517:comment:540}

      - README.md opens with headings + nested lists (smoke 1).
      - #42-style line-number anchor scopes into the containing node (smoke 4).
      - #Heading-style anchor uses exact -> prefix -> substring fallback (smoke 3).
      - Heading cursor preview spans the descendant byte-range via md2ansi (#522 tests).
      - m toggles colored / raw (smoke 5).
      - V on root pages original; V on non-root pages merged temp file. E mirrors for editor (#523 tests, smoke 7).
      - Ctrl-R re-slurps from disk and rebuilds the tree (smoke 9 + TestReload).
      Recipe is ~990 lines (a bit over the 350-line aspirational sketch, mostly module docstrings/comments). 132 unit tests in test_browse_md.py; full unit suite (1825 tests) green.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Combined-regex block parser {#519}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 09:50:58 UTC

    Lift verbatim from `md2ansi.py`:
    * `_MD_H1`..`_MD_H6` (md2ansi.py:697-702)
    * `_MD_HR` (md2ansi.py:704)
    * `_MD_CODE_GEN` (md2ansi.py:717; matches both ``` and ~~~)
    * `_MD_BLOCKQUOTE` (md2ansi.py:719)
    * `_MD_TABLE` (md2ansi.py:721)
    * `_MD_LIST` (md2ansi.py:723-726)

    Define `_MD_FRONTMATTER` per spec: `\A---\n.*?\n---(?:\n|$)`
    (anchored to file start via `\A`, DOTALL-friendly). Follow
    md2ansi's no-rollback regex discipline (every alternation has
    disjoint branches; tempered-greedy for cross-line spans).

    Build `_RULES = ((name, pat), ...)` in this order (precedence
    matters — earlier rules mask later ones inside their span):
    `h1..h6, hr, frontmatter, code, blockquote, table, list`.

    Compile combined regex via the md2ansi `_m2a_build_context` shape:
    `re.compile('|'.join(f'(?P<{n}>{p})' for n,p in _RULES),
                 re.VERBOSE | re.MULTILINE | re.DOTALL)`.

    Implement `_parse(text)` that walks `_PARSER_RE.finditer(text)`
    and emits flat parser events keyed by `m.lastgroup`. Headings
    emit one node each. List blocks delegate to the walker (#3).
    Code / blockquote / table / hr / frontmatter emit nothing (they
    exist only to mask their contents from later rules).

    Build a byte-to-line index once, ahead of `_parse`, so heading
    nodes know their `line_offset`. Exact data structure is an
    implementation choice.

    Done when: parsing a small markdown file with headings produces
    a flat ordered list of heading nodes with correct `byte_offset`
    and `line_offset`; code-fenced and quoted lines do not produce
    spurious heading nodes.

    * ## Comments {#519:comments}

      * Implemented block parser in recipes/browse-md: {#519:comment:526}

        - Lifted _MD_H1..H6, _MD_HR, _MD_CODE_GEN, _MD_BLOCKQUOTE, _MD_TABLE, _MD_LIST from md2ansi.py:697-726, converting (?P<*...>...) inner placeholders to non-capturing (?:...) per the ticket guidance.
        - Defined _MD_FRONTMATTER as a tempered-greedy \A-anchored pattern: \A---\n (?:(?! ^---[ \t]*$) [\s\S])* ^---[ \t]*(?:\n|\Z). Uses the same no-rollback shape as the fenced-code body so the engine never backtracks.
        - _RULES order: h1..h6, hr, frontmatter, code, blockquote, table, list (precedence falls out of order).
        - Compiled _PARSER_RE with VERBOSE|MULTILINE|DOTALL via the md2ansi _m2a_build_context shape.
        - Byte-to-line index: _line_starts(text) scans once to build a list of line-start offsets; _line_of() does bisect_right - 1.
        - _parse(text) yields (kind, payload) tuples: heading payloads are {'byte_offset','line_offset','text'} dicts; lists emit ('list', match) sentinels for ticket #520's per-item walker; code/blockquote/table/hr/frontmatter emit nothing.
        - get_children is left as the existing stub per ticket scope.
        Smoke test confirmed: a sample with frontmatter, H1-H4, a fenced code block containing '# fake heading', a blockquote containing '> # also fake', and a 4-line list produces exactly 4 heading events + 1 list event. Source slice at each heading's byte_offset starts with '#'. line_offset matches line_starts[lo] == byte_offset. Edge cases (--- mid-doc, fm then heading, bare --- with no closing) all correct.

  * ## Ticket: Task: List-block walker, boundaries, tree linking, Item construction {#520}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 10:23:25 UTC

    Per-list-block walk (the only rule that fans out into multiple
    emitted nodes per match):
    * Input: one `_MD_LIST` match.
    * For each line in the match: run
      `re.match(r'^([ \t]*)([-*+]|\d+\.)[ \t]+(.*)$', ln)`
      (same shape as `_m2a_fmt_list`, md2ansi.py:493).
    * On match, emit one list-item node with
      `level = len(indent.expandtabs(4)) // 2`, `kind = 'ol'` if
      marker is `\d+.` else `'ul'`, plus `byte_offset` /
      `line_offset` derived from the line's position within the
      match.

    Boundary rule — single pass over the flat node list:
    * For each node at index `i`, find next sibling-or-shallower:
      heading at level ≤ L (for headings), or list-item at indent
      ≤ L OR next heading at any level (for list items).
    * `byte_size = nodes[j].byte_offset - nodes[i].byte_offset` if
      such `j` exists, else `len(_FILE_TEXT) - nodes[i].byte_offset`.
    * `line_size` computed identically over line offsets.

    Tree linking — two stack passes:
    * Heading stack of `(level, node)`. Each new heading H at level
      L: pop entries with level ≥ L, attach H to stack top (or root
      if empty), push (L, H).
    * List stack: same mechanic on indent level. Reset on every
      heading boundary. List items attach to the nearest open list
      ancestor with strictly smaller indent, else to the surrounding
      heading (or root) if none.

    Item construction:
    * Heading nodes: `id = f'{path}#{line_offset}'`, `title` = source
      line with `.rstrip('\n')` + leading whitespace stripped (no
      `#`-stripping). `tag = 'h1'..'h6'`. `tag_style` by level: h1
      red, h2 yellow, h3 green, h4 blue, h5 magenta, h6 gray.
    * List-item nodes: same id shape. `title` = source marker line
      stripped of leading whitespace + trailing newline only.
      `tag = 'ul'` for `[-*+]`, `'ol'` for `\d+.`. `tag_style = 'dim'`.
    * Hidden attrs on every Item: `byte_offset`, `byte_size`,
      `line_offset`, `line_size`, `kind` (`'heading'`/`'list-item'`
      /`'root'`), `level`. `has_children` set from child list.

    Wire `get_children(item_id, *, reload=False)` to return cached
    children per item.

    Done when: opening a markdown file with mixed headings and lists
    shows a correctly nested tree (sub-headings under their parent
    heading; nested list items under their parent list item; list
    items under their containing heading or root).

    * ## Comments {#520:comments}

      * Smoke-tested against the ticket's sample markdown and the project README. Tree shape on the sample matches the expected layout from the ticket: {#520:comment:533}

        root
        ├── [h1] # H1
        │   ├── [h2] ## H2a
        │   │   ├── [ul] - list a1
        │   │   │   ├── [ul] - nested a1.1
        │   │   │   └── [ul] - nested a1.2
        │   │   └── [ul] - list a2
        │   └── [h2] ## H2b
        │       ├── [ol] 1. ordered b1
        │       └── [ol] 2. ordered b2
        └── [h1] # H1 again
            └── [ul] - top-level list under H1-again
        Byte-size assertion: every heading slice starts with the correct number of '#' chars. h1 slice covers bo=0..104 (everything up to the second h1); h2 slice ends at the next h2 boundary; deepest list items get the trailing bytes they own.
        End-to-end via './browse-tui --run-py recipes/browse-md ...' confirmed: tags ([h1]/[h2]/[ul]/[ol]) render, indent is correct, '▶'/'▼' markers track has_children, expanding cascades through the full tree.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Lookup contract and anchor resolution {#521}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 10:33:21 UTC

    Build the line→item lookup once at parse time:
    * `_BY_LINE: dict[int, Item]` — `line_offset` → node for every
      parsed node.
    * Whatever auxiliary structure is needed to support `_node_at_line`
      efficiently (sorted-keys list + bisect is the obvious choice;
      micro-implementation is up to the implementer).

    Implement `_node_at_line(n) -> Item | None`:
    * Exact match in `_BY_LINE` wins.
    * Otherwise return the node with the greatest `line_offset` ≤ `n`.
    * Return `None` if `n` precedes every parsed node.

    Anchor resolution (called after `_parse`, before `Browser(...)`):
    * No anchor → `initial_scope = root_id`.
    * All-digit anchor → `int(anchor)` → `_node_at_line(n)`. If
      `None`, fall through to root.
    * Non-digit anchor → three-tier heading-title match. Define
      `display_title(node)` = source line with `#` markers AND
      leading/trailing whitespace stripped (used for matching only;
      the stored `title` keeps `#`s). For each tier, scan headings
      in source order and take the first hit:
        1. Exact: `display_title == anchor`.
        2. Prefix: `display_title.startswith(anchor)`.
        3. Substring: `anchor in display_title`.
      No match in any tier → stderr warning, fall through to root.

    Done when: `recipes/browse-md FILE.md#0` opens at the first
    item, `#999999` falls back to root, `#some-heading` opens scoped
    into the matching heading.

    * ## Comments {#521:comments}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Preview pipeline and m / M toggles {#522}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 10:41:30 UTC

    `get_preview(item_id)`:
    * Root id (no `#`) → return `_FILE_TEXT`.
    * `<path>#<n>` id → resolve via `_BY_LINE` (or `_node_at_line`

      `if not callable: _md2ansi_fn = None` fallback.

      available.

      `Browser(...)`, used for `preview_width` lookup.
    * In `get_preview`, when `_MD_COLOR` is on, pipe slice through
      `_md2ansi_fn(text, line_width=(_BROWSER.preview_width or 80))`.
      Wrap the call in `try/except` and fall back to the raw slice on
      any error (matches browse-fs convention).

    `_action_toggle_md(ctx)` action bound to `m` (only if
    `_md2ansi_fn` is not None):
    * Flip `_MD_COLOR`.
    * `ctx.drop_preview_cache()`.
    * `ctx.message(f'md preview: ...')`.

    `_action_md_preview(ctx)` action bound to `M` — always available:

      from browse-claude (`recipes/browse-claude:4401-4467`).

    preview of a heading shows the heading + all descendants
    rendered with md2ansi colours; preview of root shows the whole

  * ## Ticket: Task: Source actions V / E with multi-select range merging {#523}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 09:39:41 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 10:47:19 UTC

    Lift the shape of browse-claude's `_run_source_command` /
    `_action_view_source` / `_action_edit_source` (lines
    4323-4392), swapping the per-line extractor for byte-range
    slicing.

    Target resolution:
    * `targets = ctx.targets` (handles selection-or-cursor).
    * Walk targets, classifying each as root (id has no `#`) or
      non-root.
    * If any target is root → behave as if only root was selected:
      `ctx.run_external(cmd + [<abs_path>])`. Edits via `E` persist
      naturally.
    * All targets non-root → see range merging below.

    Range merging for non-root multi-select:
    * Collect `(byte_offset, byte_size)` from each target Item.
    * Sort ascending by `byte_offset`.
    * Merge overlapping or adjacent ranges: walk the sorted list,
      extend current range when next range's `byte_offset` ≤
      current end. Result is non-overlapping, in file order.
    * Concatenate `_FILE_TEXT[bo:bo+bs]` for each merged range. If
      the previous slice doesn't end in `\n`, insert one before the
      next slice; otherwise no separator (just adjacency).
    * Write to `tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix='.md',
      delete=False, encoding='utf-8', errors='surrogateescape')`.
    * `ctx.run_external(cmd + [tmp_path])`. Unlink in `finally`.

    `_action_view_source` → uses `$PAGER` or `less -R`.
    `_action_edit_source` → uses `$EDITOR` or `vim`.
    Both call a shared `_run_source_command(ctx, env_var, default)`.

    Bind: `Action('V', ..., _action_view_source, 'none')`,
    `Action('E', ..., _action_edit_source, 'none')`. `'none'` gate
    so they fire on scope_root rows too (where `ctx.cursor` is None).

    Done when: `V` on root pages the original file; `V` on a single
    non-root item pages a temp file with that item's source slice;
    `V` with three non-root items multi-selected pages a temp file
    containing the merged/sorted ranges (no duplication, file
    order); `E` on root edits the original file in place.

    * ## Comments {#523:comments}

      * Implemented V/E source actions in recipes/browse-md. {#523:comment:538}

        Added helpers near the bottom of the recipe (just above main()):
        - _split_cmd(s): shell-split via shlex (verbatim from browse-claude:4395-4398).
        - _merge_ranges(ranges): sort + dedupe + adjacency-merge (bo, bs) tuples.
        - _write_range_excerpts(ranges): concatenate _FILE_TEXT slices into a tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix='.md', delete=False, encoding='utf-8', errors='surrogateescape'); inserts '\n' between consecutive slices only when the previous slice doesn't end in '\n'.
        - _run_source_command(ctx, env_var, default): ctx.targets → empty short-circuits; any root in targets → ctx.run_external(cmd + [root.id]); else merge ranges, write tempfile, run_external, unlink in finally swallowing OSError.
        - _action_view_source / _action_edit_source: thin wrappers over PAGER/less -R and EDITOR/vim.
        Wiring in main(): appended Action('V', ..., 'none') and Action('E', ..., 'none') to the actions list — 'none' gate so they fire on the scope_root row where ctx.cursor is None.
        Tests: added 3 new test classes to test/unit/test_browse_md.py — TestMergeRanges (9), TestWriteRangeExcerpts (6), TestRunSourceCommand (8). Total: 119 tests, all green.
        Smoke checks:
        - Scratch script against README.md with a fake ctx confirmed: root V → less -R <abs path>; single heading → less -R <tmp.md> with that section; 3 out-of-order non-root targets → tempfile with merged ranges in file order matching the expected concatenation; root E → vim <abs path>; empty targets → no run_external call.

    `## My **bold** heading` → title `My **bold** heading`.

    once stored titles are pre-stripped, `_display_title` is redundant
    and can collapse to a `.strip()` (or just the raw title). Decide

    anchor-match flow keeps working.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Lists default off; -l / --list / --lists turns them on {#543}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 20:01:32 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 21:42:23 UTC

    Argv parsing: in addition to the existing positional, accept
    `-l` / `--list` / `--lists` (any of the three forms) as a boolean
    flag. The presence of the flag means "parse list items as tree
    elements"; absence means "skip list items, headings only".

    Implementation choice: cleanest is to add a module-level
    `_INCLUDE_LISTS = False` and gate list emission. Either skip the
    `_walk_list` fan-out inside `_parse`, OR drop list events in
    `_build_nodes`. Spec-wise it doesn't matter; pick the simpler one.
    The masking properties of the `list` rule in `_PARSER_RE` must
    NOT change — code-fence vs list-line precedence still matters
    even when lists aren't emitted.

    The flag must be parsed BEFORE the positional. Order in argv
    should be flexible: `browse-md -l FILE.md` and
    `browse-md FILE.md -l` should both work. Use a small hand-rolled
    pop-flag pass (similar to browse-claude's `_pop_flag` /
    `_pop_value`) rather than reaching for argparse.

    Update `_HELP_INTRO` and the module docstring to document the flag.

    Tests:
    - `TestArgvFlag`: parse argv with and without the flag, in
      various positions, confirm `_INCLUDE_LISTS` is set correctly.
    - `TestBuildNodes` (existing): split into the lists-on case
      (existing fixture, lists present) and a lists-off case
      (`_INCLUDE_LISTS=False`, list items absent from the tree, but
      the headings unchanged).

    Done when: `browse-md FILE.md` shows headings only; `browse-md -l
    FILE.md` shows headings + lists; both forms work with
    `--list` and `--lists` aliases.

    * ## Comments {#543:comments}

      * Implemented -l/--list/--lists flag. {#543:comment:546}

        Recipe changes (recipes/browse-md):
        - Added module-level _INCLUDE_LISTS = False (production default: headings only).
        - Added _pop_flag(name, alts=()) helper, patterned after browse-claude's _pop_flag — walks sys.argv removing every match of name or any alts entry; returns True if any match was found.
        - Gated _walk_list inside _parse on _INCLUDE_LISTS. Regex masking unchanged: list span still consumed so code-fence vs list-line precedence is preserved.
        - main() now calls _pop_flag('-l', alts=('--list','--lists')) BEFORE reading the positional, so argv ordering is flexible.
        - Updated _USAGE, _HELP_INTRO, and module docstring to document the flag.
        Test changes (test/unit/test_browse_md.py):
        - _load_recipe() now takes include_lists=True (default) and sets m._INCLUDE_LISTS after exec — most existing tests assume lists-on.
        - TestArgvFlag (new): 7 tests covering absent flag, short before/after positional, --list, --lists, repeated flags, and unrelated args.
        - TestBuildNodesNoLists (new): 9 tests covering events-have-only-headings, no ul/ol in tree, no ul/ol in _BY_ID, heading ids unchanged, heading byte_offsets unchanged, H2a section subsumes list bytes, last section runs to EOF, has_children reflects no list kids.

        - 'browse-md README.md' → 9 headings, 0 list items in events.
        - 'browse-md -l README.md' → 9 headings, 5 list items.

* ## Ticket: Task: browse-md bugs {#549}

  Three user-reported bugs after the UX refinements in #541.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Non-existent file argument prints usage instead of an error {#550}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 21:47:44 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 22:02:56 UTC

    `browse-md /no/such/path.md` currently prints just the usage line
    and exits 2. That's the same output as `browse-md` (no args at
    all), which is confusing — the user gave an argument that just
    happens to point at a missing file.

    Expected: distinct error message that names the missing path,
    e.g. `browse-md: no such file: /no/such/path.md` (then exit 2,
    optionally followed by the usage line on a separate stderr
    write).

    Fix in `recipes/browse-md`'s `main()` argv-parsing block. Add a
    test in `TestArgvFlag` (or a new `TestArgvErrors` class) that
    captures stderr and asserts the error message format.

    * ## Comments {#550:comments}

      * Replaced bare _USAGE fallthrough with _die('no such file: ...', with_usage=False). Echoes the user's input pre-expanduser. Added test_missing_file_path_reports_path_without_usage. {#550:comment:556}

  * ## Ticket: Task: Unknown options and extra positionals should error, not be ignored {#551}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 21:47:44 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 22:02:56 UTC

    `browse-md --bogus FILE.md` and `browse-md FILE.md extra` both
    silently accept the unrecognised tokens today (the flag-popper
    leaves them in `sys.argv`, the positional grabs `sys.argv[1]`,
    everything else is dropped). The user gets no signal that their
    command line was wrong.

    Expected: any unrecognised `-` / `--` token, or any extra
    positional beyond the file, prints an error to stderr (e.g.
    `browse-md: unrecognised option: --bogus` or
    `browse-md: unexpected argument: extra`) and exits 2. The usage
    line should follow.

    Implementation: after `_pop_flag` consumes the known flags,
    inspect what's left in `sys.argv[1:]`. Exactly one positional
    is expected; anything else is an error. Flag-shaped leftovers
    (anything starting with `-`) should be reported as
    "unrecognised option" specifically.

    Tests in `TestArgvFlag` / new `TestArgvErrors`: various malformed
    argvs assert the error-and-exit behaviour. Capture stderr.

    * ## Comments {#551:comments}

      * Added _die helper and post-_pop_flag leftover-arg validation: '-'-prefixed leftovers => 'unrecognised option', extra non-'-' positionals => 'unexpected argument', zero positionals => 'missing FILE.md[#anchor]'. New TestArgvErrors covers all paths. {#551:comment:557}

  * ## Ticket: Task: V / E on the root row crashes with AttributeError on byte_offset {#552}

        status: done
        created: 2026-05-28 21:47:44 UTC
        updated: 2026-05-28 21:56:54 UTC

    Pressing `V` or `E` on the synthetic root row (the scope-root
    pseudo-row at the top of the listing pane) raises:

    ```
    File "recipes/browse-md", line 931, in _run_source_command
      ranges = [(t.byte_offset, t.byte_size) for t in targets]
    AttributeError: 'Item' object has no attribute 'byte_offset'
    ```

    Diagnosis: `_run_source_command` checks each target for
    `kind == 'root'` via `getattr(item, 'kind', None) == 'root'`. The
    framework's scope_root pseudo-row is a different Item from our
    underlying root Item — it doesn't carry our hidden `kind` /
    `byte_offset` / `byte_size` attrs. The classifier therefore
    misses it and the function falls through to the byte-range
    branch, which then explodes on the missing `byte_offset`.

    Expected: `V` on the scope-root row pages the original file (as
    documented). `E` on it opens the original file in `$EDITOR`.

    Fix options to investigate:
    * Detect the scope-root pseudo-row explicitly. The framework
      either exposes a flag on the pseudo-item (look in `docs/api.md`
      or `src-tui/`) or the pseudo-item's `id` matches the absolute
      file path — same id as our real root Item, so a lookup in
      `_BY_ID` and an `is`/equality check against the stored root
      would work.
    * Alternatively: classify targets defensively. Treat any item
      that's not in `_BY_ID`, or any item that maps to our root, as
      "root" for the purposes of `_run_source_command`.

    Tests: extend `TestRunSourceCommand` with a target-list that
    contains a "scope-root-like" Item (no `kind`, no `byte_offset`)
    and assert the function takes the root-wins path. Also a UI-
    level smoke check via the existing pty harness if one's
    available.

    This is the highest-priority of the three bugs (a crash, not a
    misleading exit code).

    * ## Comments {#552:comments}

      * Reproduced via test_loader: a synthetic Item with id=path but no kind/byte_offset triggered the AttributeError on line 934. Root cause: browse-md always launches scoped (initial_scope=root.id), the framework's _find_item can't locate the root in any cached _children list (root is the tree apex, never a child), so visible_items fabricates a scope-root pseudo-Item with id=path, has_children=True, synthetic=True but NO kind/byte_offset/byte_size — the recipe-attached hidden attrs the V/E classifier relied on. {#552:comment:554}

        Fix: in _run_source_command, classify root by id-match (it.id == _ROOT_PATH) in addition to kind=='root'. Both checks needed: kind=='root' handles the real root Item path; the id check catches the framework's scope-root pseudo-row. Use root_target.id (not _ROOT_PATH) in the dispatch so the tests that don't set _ROOT_PATH continue to work — they're equal in production but root_target.id is the invariant carried by both Item flavours.
        Tests: extended TestRunSourceCommand with a _ScopeRootPseudoItem helper class (no kind/byte_offset/byte_size, mirrors the framework's fabrication) and two cases: pseudo alone routes to root path, pseudo mixed with non-root still wins root. setUp/tearDown also patch and restore _ROOT_PATH and _BY_ID per ticket instruction. 162 tests pass (was 160; +2).
        CLI smoke under tmux: launched recipes/browse-md README.md, pressed V on the top (scope-root) row — pager opened on the file (PAGER=cat output rendered), no traceback. Pressed E on the top row with EDITOR=true — fired and returned cleanly, no traceback. Pressed V on first heading (non-root path) — still goes through the byte-range merge branch, no traceback.

* ## Ticket: Task: Multiple markdown files on the command line {#553}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-28 21:50:44 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-28 22:18:44 UTC

  Today `browse-md` takes exactly one positional. Extend it to
  accept multiple file paths, surfaced as siblings under the root.

  Argv shape:
  ```
  browse-md [-l] FILE1.md [FILE2.md ...]
  browse-md [-l] FILE1.md#anchor [FILE2.md ...]    # anchor still
                                                   # applies to FILE1
  ```

  Each file is parsed independently with the existing pipeline
  (parser → `_build_nodes` → byte-to-line index). Each file
  becomes a top-level subtree under the synthetic root: a per-file
  Item that owns the file's headings (and lists, when `-l` is on).

  Tree model with N files:
  ```
  <synthetic-root>          id = something stable, e.g. literal "(multi)"
                            or the joined paths; title = something
                            short. Preview = ??? (see below.)
  ├── FILE1.md              id = abs path of FILE1
  │   ├── # H1
  │   ├── # H2
  │   └── ...
  ├── FILE2.md
  │   └── ...
  └── ...
  ```

  Per-file Items now occupy what was previously the single synthetic
  root. Each carries its own `_FILE_TEXT`, `_BY_LINE`, etc.

  Open questions to resolve in implementation (the design doc can
  stay quiet — these are recipe-level details):

  * **`_FILE_TEXT` plurality.** The cleanest refactor is a single
    `_FILES: dict[str, FileState]` keyed by abs-path, where
    `FileState` carries `text`, `by_line`, `lines_sorted`, etc. The
    module-level globals `_FILE_TEXT` / `_BY_LINE` / `_LINES_SORTED`
    go away — every lookup site routes through `_FILES[path]`.
  * **Root preview.** With one file the root previews the whole
    file. With N files, root preview should probably show a
    summary (`FILE1.md  (12 headings)\nFILE2.md  (5 headings)`),
    not a concatenation. Pick whichever fits the existing preview
    flow and is least surprising.
  * **`V` / `E` on root.** No single original file to open. Either
    error gracefully (`browse-md: V/E on multi-root is ambiguous`),
    or open the file the cursor's parent chain belongs to. Simplest
    sensible choice: take the first file passed on the command line.
  * **Reload (Ctrl-R).** Each file reparses independently. `_reparse`
    should iterate over `_FILES`.
  * **Anchor on positional.** `#anchor` only attaches to the first
    file (we don't bother trying to disambiguate per-file anchors
    in argv). Document this in `_HELP_INTRO`.
  * **`_node_at_line` and IDs.** Item ids are still `<abs_path>#<n>`
    — already unique across files since abs paths differ. The
    line-bisect lookup needs to consult the right file's index
    (`_FILES[path].lines_sorted`).
  * **Help text.** Update `_HELP_INTRO`, module docstring, `_USAGE`.

  Tests:
  * `TestArgvMulti`: argv with two and three files, with `-l`,
    with `-l` interleaved (`-l FILE1 FILE2` and `FILE1 -l FILE2`),
    with `FILE1#anchor FILE2` (anchor only on first).
  * `TestBuildNodesMulti`: build with two files, assert the root
    has two children whose `id` is the abs path of each file,
    each subtree contains the expected headings.
  * `TestReloadMulti`: modify both files on disk, Ctrl-R, both
    reparsed.

  Done when: `browse-md a.md b.md` opens with two top-level
  subtrees; navigating, previewing, and `V`/`E` all work; `m`/`M`
  still toggle preview rendering; existing single-file tests
  still pass.

  * ## Comments {#553:comments}

    * Amendment (2026-05-28): If no anchors are present in argv, the initial view is the normal root. Whenever at least one positional carries an anchor, the initial scope drills into the first ANCHORED file (in argv order — not necessarily the first positional). So 'browse-md a.md b.md' opens at root; 'browse-md a.md b.md#foo' drills into b.md#foo; 'browse-md a.md#x b.md#y' drills into a.md#x (first anchor wins). _HELP_INTRO should document this. {#553:comment:555}

    * Implemented multi-file support for browse-md. {#553:comment:558}

      State refactor:
      - Added FileState dataclass holding per-file (text, line_starts, by_id, by_line, lines_sorted, file_root).
      - _FILES dict[str, FileState] keyed by abs path; _INPUT_FILES list of (path, anchor) tuples preserves argv order.
      - Synthetic multi-root with id='(multi)' and kind='multi-root' built only when len(_FILES)>1; single-file mode uses the per-file root as Browser root (legacy behaviour).
      - _BY_ID is the aggregate index (multi-root + every file's by_id).
      - Per-Item back-reference: item.file_path = path lets get_preview slice the right file.
      - Legacy single-file shims (_FILE_TEXT, _BY_LINE, _LINES_SORTED, _ROOT_PATH) mirror the FIRST file's state for back-compat with tests that populate them directly.
      - _classify_id(node_id) is the single classifier — returns ('multi-root'|'file-root'|'content'|'unknown', path_or_None). Used by get_preview and _run_source_command.
      Argv:
      - main() walks every positional, splits on first '#', validates each file. Missing file surfaces the user's input verbatim.
      - First-anchor-wins: first non-empty anchor in argv order seeds initial_scope; subsequent anchors recorded but ignored.
      Anchor:
      - _resolve_anchor(anchor, file_root_id) — derives the right file_state from _FILES, scans only that file's headings. Legacy single-file callers (tests) fall back to module-level _BY_ID with file_path filtering.
      - _node_at_line(n, file_state=None) — file_state=None falls back to legacy globals.
      V/E semantics:
      - Multi-root target -> opens FIRST input file (documented in _HELP_INTRO).
      - Per-file root target -> opens that file directly.
      - Same-file non-root targets -> merged byte-range tempfile.
      - Cross-file multi-select -> FIRST argv file's targets only (documented).
      - Scope-root pseudo-Item with id=_ROOT_ID classifies as multi-root.
      Tests: 207 total (168 existing + 39 new across TestArgvMulti, TestBuildMulti, TestAnchorMulti, TestGetPreviewMulti, TestRunSourceCommandMulti, TestReloadMulti, TestClassifyId). All green. One existing test (test_extra_positional) updated to test_extra_positional_nonexistent_file since 'extra' now treated as another file positional.
      Full unit-test suite (1900 tests across the project) also green.
      CLI smoke (pseudo-TTY): two files render as multi-root '2 files' + two subtrees; anchor on file 2 drills into that file's section; anchor on file 1 drills into file 1; single-file mode unchanged; missing file mid-list dies with user-input path.

* ## Ticket: Task: Drop the synthetic multi-root; files ARE the root entries {#559}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-28 22:23:05 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-28 22:33:18 UTC

  Today multi-file mode wraps the per-file roots under a synthetic
  `_ROOT_ID = '(multi)'` Item. That's an extra layer the user has
  to step into. browse-claude's pattern is the right one: pass
  `root_id=None` to BrowserConfig, and have `get_children(None)`
  return the top-level entries directly.

  Apply that to browse-md:
  * `BrowserConfig(root_id=None, ...)` always.
  * `get_children(None, *, reload=False)` returns the list of
    per-file roots in argv order.
  * Drop `_ROOT_ID`, the `'multi-root'` Item, and the
    `'multi-root'` branch of `_classify_id`.

  Single-file UX must be preserved: with one file and no anchor,
  the browser should start scoped INTO the file (showing its
  headings), exactly as it does today. Implementation:
  * Multi-file, no anchor → `initial_scope = None` (top-level
    list of files visible).
  * Multi-file, first anchor on file X → `initial_scope =
    _resolve_anchor(...)` against file X (unchanged).
  * Single-file, no anchor → `initial_scope = file_root.id`
    (the file root, same visual as before).
  * Single-file, anchor → `initial_scope = _resolve_anchor(...)`
    (unchanged).

  Multi-root preview, multi-root `V`/`E` "open first file" rules,
  and the cross-file multi-select "first-file wins" rule all go
  away — they only existed because of the synthetic root. With
  files at the top, there's no row that needs ambiguous-target
  resolution.

  Spec doc: update the "Tree model" section to remove the
  synthetic multi-root level. Help text: update accordingly.

  Tests:
  * `TestBuildMulti`: assert no `'multi-root'` Item; assert
    `get_children(None)` returns the per-file roots in argv order.
  * `TestAnchorMulti`: no-anchor case asserts `initial_scope is
    None`. Single-file no-anchor case asserts `initial_scope ==
    file_root.id`. Anchored cases unchanged.
  * `TestGetPreviewMulti`: drop the multi-root summary test;
    `get_preview(None)` is the framework's concern, not ours
    (depending on framework — if it asks, return ''). Per-file
    root preview = whole file (unchanged).
  * `TestRunSourceCommandMulti`: drop the multi-root cases; the
    per-file-root cases stay (V/E on a file row opens that file).
  * `_classify_id` tests: drop the multi-root case.
  * `TestArgvMulti` / `TestReloadMulti`: unchanged behaviour.

  Done when: `browse-md a.md b.md` shows two top-level rows
  (no `(multi)` row above them); single-file `browse-md a.md`
  opens scoped into the file's headings exactly as before;
  anchor flows still work.

  * ## Comments {#559:comments}

    * Implemented. Dropped synthetic multi-root from recipes/browse-md. {#559:comment:560}

      Files changed:
      - recipes/browse-md: removed _ROOT_ID, _build_multi_root, _multi_root_preview, _pick_path_for_root; added _write_range_excerpts_grouped; updated _classify_id (dropped multi-root branch); rewrote _run_source_command (no multi-root short-circuit, cross-file selections honoured); main() now passes BrowserConfig(root_id=None) with initial_scope = None / file_root.id / resolved-anchor per the four cases; get_children(None) returns per-file roots in argv order; get_preview(None) returns ''; module docstring + _HELP_INTRO updated.

* ## Ticket: Task: First preview fetch on startup runs with width=0, recipes fall back to 80 {#561}

      updated: 2026-05-28 22:52:45 UTC
      status: done
      created: 2026-05-28 22:51:12 UTC

  BUG
  ====
  On initial load, the first entry's preview pane is rendered as if it were 80 columns
  wide regardless of the actual terminal width.

  Root cause (`040-state.py`, `Browser.run`):

    - line 5897:  ``self.post(self._do_initial_fetch)``
    - line 5900:  ``run_until_idle(0.5)``  — wait for tree
    - line 5903:  ``self._update_preview_for_cursor()``  — request preview
    - line 5906:  ``run_until_idle(0.2)``  — preview worker calls
                  ``get_preview`` here; recipes read ``preview_width``
                  which is still ``0`` (no paint has computed the layout
                  yet), so the ``or 80`` fallback kicks in and the markdown
                  wrap is sized to 80 columns.
    - line 5920:  ``render_full(self)``  — only here does ``_layout_for``
                  run and set ``browser._preview_width`` to the real value,
                  but the preview text has already been cached at width 80.

  Fix: compute the layout (which sets ``_preview_width`` as a side-effect)
  before the initial ``_update_preview_for_cursor`` kick, so the first
  ``get_preview`` reads the correct width and the cached render matches the
  pane.

  After a SIGWINCH or any later key the preview cache is invalidated and
  rewrapped at the live width, so the bug is only visible on the *very
  first* paint. Still worth fixing — that first impression is what users
  see.

  * ## Ticket: Task: Write failing test: preview worker sees the real preview_width on first fetch {#562}

      - `_state.term_size`  → patch `term_size` to return a non-default geometry, e.g. (160, 40), so the preview pane width is unambiguous (not coincidentally 80).

    In `src-tui/040-state.py`, inside `Browser.run()` between the first `run_until_idle` and `_update_preview_for_cursor` (around line 5902), call `_layout_for(self)` so that the preview-pane width is computed and cached on the Browser before the worker reads it.

* ## Ticket: Single-file: auto-expand file row instead of scoping in {#566}

      status: done
      created: 2026-05-29 00:24:14 UTC
      updated: 2026-05-29 00:29:16 UTC

  Bug: single-file mode sets ``initial_scope = file_root.id``, which
  pushes one entry onto the framework's scope_stack (browse-claude
  inserts a parent scope underneath for this reason; we don't).
  Alt-up from there pops the stack to an empty/undefined state and
  the user sees an empty list.

  Fix per user direction: drop the ``initial_scope = file_root.id``
  branch entirely. Single-file no-anchor leaves ``initial_scope =
  None`` (same as multi-file no-anchor). Auto-expand the file's
  top-level row so the headings are visible immediately — the
  same visual the old single-file UX produced, without the
  scope-stack hack.

  Apply ``b.expand(file_root.id)`` (or whatever the public API
  expects) AFTER ``Browser(...)`` construction and BEFORE
  ``b.run()``, only when ``len(_FILES) == 1`` and ``_ANCHOR`` is
  empty. Multi-file or anchored cases stay as-is.

  Anchored single-file (FILE.md#foo) still drills into the
  anchor — that path is independent.

  Tests:
  * Update existing tests that asserted ``initial_scope ==
    file_root.id`` to assert ``initial_scope is None`` AND that
    the auto-expand call landed on the right id (via a mock).
  * Add a new case: single-file with anchor leaves
    ``initial_scope`` resolved (auto-expand NOT applied — anchor
    drill-in already shows the heading).
  * Add a case: multi-file no anchor still no auto-expand.

  Done when: ``browse-md a.md`` shows the file row at top with
  headings already visible beneath it; alt-up from a heading
  scopes back to the files level (one row visible, not empty);
  multi-file behaviour unchanged; anchored behaviour unchanged.

  * ## Comments {#566:comments}

    * Implemented per ticket: dropped initial_scope=file_root.id branch entirely. Single-file no-anchor now leaves initial_scope=None and calls b.expand(file_root.id) after Browser() construction (before b.run()). Multi-file and anchored paths unchanged. {#566:comment:567}

      Updated test stub: _Stub split into _Stub + _BrowserStub. _BrowserStub stashes the BrowserConfig positional arg on self.config and records expand(...) calls on self.expand_calls.
      TestAnchorMulti updates:
      * _initial_scope helper updated — single-file no-anchor branch removed (now returns None).
      * test_single_file_no_anchor_returns_file_root_id renamed to test_single_file_no_anchor_returns_none, asserts initial_scope is None.
      * Added test_single_file_no_anchor_auto_expands_file_row — drives main() and asserts config.initial_scope is None AND b.expand was called once with the file's root id.
      * Added test_single_file_with_anchor_does_not_auto_expand — config.initial_scope resolves to anchored heading, b.expand NOT called.
      * Added test_multi_file_no_anchor_does_not_auto_expand — config.initial_scope is None, b.expand NOT called.

      created: 2026-05-29 01:24:02 UTC

  User reports: in browse-md, multi-selecting items via space-mark
  and pressing V or E shows only the cursor item, not the
  selection. Expected: V/E operate on the whole selection (per
  the existing `_run_source_command` logic using `ctx.targets`).

  Suspects:
  * `ctx.targets` may not be returning what the recipe thinks —
    check whether `ctx.selected` is populated in browse-md at the
    moment V/E fire. Compare with browse-claude where the same
    pattern works.
  * The `'none'` gate may interact with selection state — verify
    by changing the gate to `'targets'` (or just leaving it
    `'none'` but adding a diagnostic).
  * Selection may be scope-bound and the scope-root pseudo-Item
    auto-expand from #566 may interact with it.

  Workflow:
  1. Reproduce. Drive the recipe through tmux: open
     `recipes/browse-md README.md`, expand the file row, space-mark
     two or three headings, press V (with `PAGER=cat`). Observe
     output.
  2. Add a transient `ctx.message(repr([t.id for t in ctx.targets]))`
     at the top of `_run_source_command` to confirm what targets is.
     Capture the message.
  3. Diagnose. Likely outcomes:
     a) `ctx.targets` IS the cursor only → framework / selection
        bug. Compare with browse-claude's selection flow.
     b) `ctx.targets` IS the selection but the merge / write
        path collapses to the cursor span somehow.
  4. Fix the underlying issue. Remove the diagnostic.
  5. Add a test that exercises the multi-select V path via the
     mock ctx — `targets` returning two items, assert
     `run_external` was called with a tempfile that contains
     BOTH ranges.
